	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Latin proverbs</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikiquote</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><p>This is a list of <b><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin" class="extiw" title="w:Latin">Latin</a> proverbs</b> and sayings.
</p><p><small>Alphabetized by first word of proverb<br />
<a href="#A">A</a> · <a href="#B">B</a> · <a href="#C">C</a> · <a href="#D">D</a> · <a href="#E">E</a> · <a href="#F">F</a> · <a href="#G">G</a> · <a href="#H">H</a> · <a href="#I">I</a> · <a href="#J">J</a> · <a href="#K">K</a> · <a href="#L">L</a> · <a href="#M">M</a> · <a href="#N">N</a> · <a href="#O">O</a> · <a href="#P">P</a> · <a href="#Q">Q</a> · <a href="#R">R</a> · <a href="#S">S</a> · <a href="#T">T</a> · <a href="#U">U</a> · <a href="#V">V</a> · <a href="#W">W</a> · <a href="#X">X</a> · <a href="#Y">Y</a> · <a href="#Z">Z</a> · <a href="#See_also">See also</a> · <a href="#References">References</a> · <a href="#External_links">External links</a></small>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="A">A</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latin_proverbs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: A">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><i>A diabolo, qui est simia dei.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Where god has a church the devil will have his chapel.</li>
<li>"Wherever God erects a house of prayer,<br />The Devil always builds a chapel there:<br />And 'twill be found, upon examination,<br />The latter has the largest congregation."</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Daniel_Defoe" title="Daniel Defoe">Daniel Defoe</a>, <i>The True-Born Englishman</i> (1701)</li>
<li>Source for proverb: <cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;874. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B874&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Abbati, medico, patrono que intima pande.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Conceal not the truth from thy physician and lawyer.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;666. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B666&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Absens haeres non erit.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Out of sight, out of mind.</li>
<li>Source: <cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1998">Strauss, Emmanuel&#32;(1998).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European Proverbs</i>. Routledge. p.&#160;16. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415160502" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415160502</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+Proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emmanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emmanuel&amp;rft.date=1998&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B16&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415160502&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Abyssus abyssum invocat.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Deep calls to deep.</li>
<li>Note: From the Bible, Psalm 42:7.</li></ul></li>
<li><i>Quidquid præcipies esto brevis.</i>
<ul><li>"Whatever advice you give, be short."</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Horace" title="Horace">Horace</a>, <i>Ars Poetica</i> (18 BC), CCCXXXV. Reported in <i>Hoyt's New Cyclopedia Of Practical Quotations</i> (1922), p. 10-11.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;695. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B695&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Acquirit qui tuetur.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Sparing is the first gaining.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFBurke2009">Burke&#32;(2009).&#32;<i>The General Armory of England, Scotland, Ireland, and Wales, Comprising a Registry of Armorial Bearings from the Earliest to the Present Time</i>. Heritage Books. p.&#160;710. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0788437208" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0788437208</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+General+Armory+of+England%2C+Scotland%2C+Ireland%2C+and+Wales%2C+Comprising+a+Registry+of+Armorial+Bearings+from+the+Earliest+to+the+Present+Time&amp;rft.aulast=Burke&amp;rft.au=Burke&amp;rft.date=2009&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B710&amp;rft.pub=Heritage+Books&amp;rft.isbn=0788437208&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Acta Non Verba.</i>
<ul><li>Translations: Deeds, not words - motto of the United States Merchant Marine Academy, at Kings Point, New York, USA.</li>
<li>English equivalents: Words are leaves, deeds are fruits.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFFuschetto2003">Fuschetto&#32;(2003).&#32;<i>Kings Point: Acta Non Verba</i>. Diversified Graphics, Incorporated.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Kings+Point%3A+Acta+Non+Verba&amp;rft.aulast=Fuschetto&amp;rft.au=Fuschetto&amp;rft.date=2003&amp;rft.pub=Diversified+Graphics%2C+Incorporated&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Ancipiti plus ferit ense gula.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Gluttony kills more than the sword.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;864. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B864&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Aegrescit medendo.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: The remedy is often worse than the disease; Burn not your house to rid it of the mouse.</li>
<li>"Action taken to put something right is often more unpleasant or damaging than the original problem."</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMartin_H._Manser2007">Martin H. Manser&#32;(2007).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=fgaUQc8NbTYC&amp;pg=PA232">The Facts on File Dictionary of Proverbs</a></i>. Infobase Publishing. p.&#160;232. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780816066735" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 978-0-8160-6673-5</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Facts+on+File+Dictionary+of+Proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Martin+H.+Manser&amp;rft.au=Martin+H.+Manser&amp;rft.date=2007&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B232&amp;rft.pub=Infobase+Publishing&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-8160-6673-5&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DfgaUQc8NbTYC%26pg%3DPA232&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFCantera_Ortiz_de_Urbina2005">Cantera Ortiz de Urbina, Jesús&#32;(16 November 2005).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=xll5lkkwNI0C&amp;pg=PA306">Refranero Latino</a></i>. Ediciones AKAL. p.&#160;306. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9788446012962" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 978-84-460-1296-2</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Refranero+Latino&amp;rft.aulast=Cantera+Ortiz+de+Urbina&amp;rft.aufirst=Jes%C3%BAs&amp;rft.au=Cantera+Ortiz+de+Urbina%2C+Jes%C3%BAs&amp;rft.date=16+November+2005&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B306&amp;rft.pub=Ediciones+AKAL&amp;rft.isbn=978-84-460-1296-2&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3Dxll5lkkwNI0C%26pg%3DPA306&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Aegroto dum anima est, spes est.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: As long as there is life there is hope.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFErasmus,_Mynors1991">Erasmus, Mynors&#32;(1991).&#32;<i>Collected Works of Erasmus: Adages II I 1 to II VI 100</i>. University of Toronto Press. p.&#160;467. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0802059546" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0802059546</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Collected+Works+of+Erasmus%3A+Adages+II+I+1+to+II+VI+100&amp;rft.aulast=Erasmus%2C+Mynors&amp;rft.au=Erasmus%2C+Mynors&amp;rft.date=1991&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B467&amp;rft.pub=University+of+Toronto+Press&amp;rft.isbn=0802059546&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Aeque pars ligni curvi ac recti valet igni.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Crooked logs make straight fires.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;683. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B683&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Age quod agis.</i>
<ul><li>Translation and English equivalent: Do what you do, in the sense of "Do well what you do", "Do well in whatever you do" or "Be serious in what you do"</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book"><i>The Nation</i>. Nation Company. 1884. p.&#160;425.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Nation&amp;rft.date=1884&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B425&amp;rft.pub=Nation+Company&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Age si quid agis.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "If there is something [quid for aliquid] you do (well), carry on", "If you do something, do it well" see also "Age quod agis"</li>
<li>English equivalent: Bloom where you are planted.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFLindsay1968">Lindsay&#32;(1968).&#32;<i>Early Latin verse</i>. Oxford U. P.. p.&#160;21.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Early+Latin+verse&amp;rft.aulast=Lindsay&amp;rft.au=Lindsay&amp;rft.date=1968&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B21&amp;rft.pub=Oxford+U.+P.&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Aliis si licet, tibi non licet.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: If others are allowed to, that does not mean you are. (see also <i>quod licet Iovi, non licet bovi</i>)</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFPatrick1810">Patrick&#32;(1810).&#32;<i>Terence's Comedies</i>. Gilbert and Hodges. p.&#160;345.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Terence%27s+Comedies&amp;rft.aulast=Patrick&amp;rft.au=Patrick&amp;rft.date=1810&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B345&amp;rft.pub=Gilbert+and+Hodges&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li>
<li><i>An nescis, mi fili, quantilla prudentia mundus regatur?</i> (alternatively: <i>regatur orbis</i>)
<ul><li>Translation: Don't you know, my son, with how little wisdom the world is governed?</li>
<li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Axel_Oxenstierna" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Axel Oxenstierna">Axel Oxenstierna</a> (1583 – 1654), 1648 letter to son, who was involved in negotiating the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peace_of_Westphalia" class="extiw" title="wikipedia:Peace of Westphalia">Peace of Westphalia</a><sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Sometimes attributed to <a href="/wiki/Cardinal_Richelieu" title="Cardinal Richelieu">Cardinal Richelieu</a>. Variant form due to <a href="/wiki/John_Selden" title="John Selden">John Selden</a></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Aliquis in omnibus est nullus in singulis.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: Someone in all, is nothing in one.</li>
<li>English equivalent: Jack of all trades, master of none; Jack of all trades begs bread on Sundays.</li>
<li>"Somebody who has a very wide range of abilities or skills usually does not excel at any of them."</li>
<li>Source for meaning of English equivalent: <cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMartin_H._Manser2007">Martin H. Manser&#32;(2007).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=fgaUQc8NbTYC&amp;pg=PA156">The Facts on File Dictionary of Proverbs</a></i>. Infobase Publishing. p.&#160;156. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780816066735" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 978-0-8160-6673-5</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Facts+on+File+Dictionary+of+Proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Martin+H.+Manser&amp;rft.au=Martin+H.+Manser&amp;rft.date=2007&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B156&amp;rft.pub=Infobase+Publishing&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-8160-6673-5&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DfgaUQc8NbTYC%26pg%3DPA156&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1998">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1998).&#32;<i>Concise Dictionary of European Proverbs</i>&#32;(Abbreviated ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;70. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415160502" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415160502</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Concise+Dictionary+of+European+Proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1998&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B70&amp;rft.edition=Abbreviated&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415160502&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Arcem ex cloacâ facĕre.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Don't make a mountain out of a molehill.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book"><i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=PdxtAAAAMAAJ&amp;pg=PA109">Proverbs of All Nations</a></i>. W. Kent &amp; Company (late D. Bogue). 1859. p.&#160;58.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Proverbs+of+All+Nations&amp;rft.date=1859&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B58&amp;rft.pub=W.+Kent+%26+Company+%28late+D.+Bogue%29&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DPdxtAAAAMAAJ%26pg%3DPA109&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Aries cornibus Iasciviens.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Better fed than taught.</li>
<li>"For if absurdity be the subject of laughter, doubt you not but great boldness is seldom without some absurdity."</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFBacon1625">Bacon, Francis&#32;(1625).&#32;<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Essays_(Francis_Bacon)" class="extiw" title="w:Essays (Francis Bacon)">Essayes or Counsels, Civill and Morall</a></i>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=%5B%5Bw%3AEssays_%28Francis_Bacon%29%7CEssayes+or+Counsels%2C+Civill+and+Morall%5D%5D&amp;rft.aulast=Bacon&amp;rft.aufirst=Francis&amp;rft.au=Bacon%2C+Francis&amp;rft.date=1625&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMawr1885">Mawr, E.B.&#32;(1885).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://editura.mttlc.ro/carti/mawr-analogous-proverbs.pdf">Analogous Proverbs in Ten Languages</a></i>. p.&#160;16.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Analogous+Proverbs+in+Ten+Languages&amp;rft.aulast=Mawr&amp;rft.aufirst=E.B.&amp;rft.au=Mawr%2C+E.B.&amp;rft.date=1885&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B16&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Feditura.mttlc.ro%2Fcarti%2Fmawr-analogous-proverbs.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Atqui, e lotio est.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: Yet it comes from urine.</li>
<li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vespasian" class="extiw" title="w:Vespasian">Emperor Vespasian</a> to his son Titus, when the latter, complaining about the former's <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/urine_tax" class="extiw" title="w:urine tax">urine tax</a>, acknowledged a coin collected had no odor.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><ul><li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFSuetonius_Tranquillus"><a href="/wiki/Suetonius" title="Suetonius">Suetonius Tranquillus, Gaius</a>&#32;(<a href="/wiki/9_December" class="mw-redirect" title="9 December">9 December</a> <a href="/wiki/2003" class="mw-disambig" title="2003">2003</a>)&#32;[121 CE].&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://penelope.uchicago.edu/Thayer/L/Roman/Texts/Suetonius/12Caesars/Vespasian*.html#23.3">"Divus Vespasianus"</a></i>. University of Chicago. pp.&#160;section 23.3, page 317<span class="reference-accessdate">.&#32;Retrieved on 2006-09-09</span>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=%22Divus+Vespasianus%22&amp;rft.aulast=Suetonius+Tranquillus&amp;rft.aufirst=Gaius&amp;rft.au=Suetonius+Tranquillus%2C+Gaius&amp;rft.date=%5B%5B9+December%5D%5D+%5B%5B2003%5D%5D&amp;rft.pages=pp.%26nbsp%3Bsection+23.3%2C+page+317&amp;rft.pub=University+of+Chicago&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fpenelope.uchicago.edu%2FThayer%2FL%2FRoman%2FTexts%2FSuetonius%2F12Caesars%2FVespasian%2A.html%2323.3&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book"><i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://penelope.uchicago.edu/Thayer/E/Roman/Texts/Suetonius/12Caesars/Vespasian*.html#23.3">"The Life of Vespasian"</a></i>. University of Chicago. <a href="/wiki/9_December" class="mw-redirect" title="9 December">9 December</a> <a href="/wiki/2003" class="mw-disambig" title="2003">2003</a><span class="reference-accessdate">.&#32;Retrieved on 2006-09-09</span>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=%22The+Life+of+Vespasian%22&amp;rft.date=%5B%5B9+December%5D%5D+%5B%5B2003%5D%5D&amp;rft.pub=University+of+Chicago&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fpenelope.uchicago.edu%2FThayer%2FE%2FRoman%2FTexts%2FSuetonius%2F12Caesars%2FVespasian%2A.html%2323.3&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Auctoritas non veritas facit legem</i>
<ul><li>Translation: Authority, not truth, makes law.</li>
<li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_Hobbes" class="extiw" title="w:Thomas Hobbes">Thomas Hobbes</a>, "<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leviathan_(book)" class="extiw" title="w:Leviathan (book)">Leviathan</a>" II, 26</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Audaces fortuna iuvat.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: Fortune favors the brave.(<a href="/wiki/Virgil" title="Virgil">Virgil</a>, <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aeneid" class="extiw" title="w:Aeneid">Aeneid</a></i> 10, 284)</li>
<li>English equivalent: Fortune favours the bold.</li>
<li>"Those who act boldly or courageously are most likely to succeed."</li>
<li>Source for meaning: <cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMartin_H._Manser2007">Martin H. Manser&#32;(2007).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=fgaUQc8NbTYC&amp;pg=PA94">The Facts on File Dictionary of Proverbs</a></i>. Infobase Publishing. p.&#160;94. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780816066735" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 978-0-8160-6673-5</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Facts+on+File+Dictionary+of+Proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Martin+H.+Manser&amp;rft.au=Martin+H.+Manser&amp;rft.date=2007&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B94&amp;rft.pub=Infobase+Publishing&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-8160-6673-5&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DfgaUQc8NbTYC%26pg%3DPA94&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Audentes fortuna juvat.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: Fortune favors the bold. (Motto of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/80th_Fighter_Squadron" class="extiw" title="w:80th Fighter Squadron">80th Fighter Squadron</a>, of the US Air Force, and of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/USS_Florida_(SSGN-728)" class="extiw" title="w:USS Florida (SSGN-728)">USS Florida</a>)</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Audi, vide, tace, si tu vis vivere (in pace).</i>
<ul><li>Translation: Hear, see, be silent, if you wish to live (in peace).  Roman proverb, according to <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.daltai.com/proverbs/weeks/week120.htm">this</a>.</li>
<li>English equivalent: Rather see than hear.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inveniam_viam" class="extiw" title="w:Inveniam viam">Aut inveniam viam aut faciam</a>.</i>
<ul><li>Alternate phrasing: Aut viam inveniam aut faciam</li>
<li>Translation: I'll either find a way or make one.</li>
<li>English equivalent: Where there's a will, there's a way.</li>
<li>"If you are sufficiently determined to achieve something, then you will find a way of doing so."</li>
<li>Source for meaning of English equivalent: <cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMartin_H._Manser2007">Martin H. Manser&#32;(2007).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=fgaUQc8NbTYC&amp;pg=PA113">The Facts on File Dictionary of Proverbs</a></i>. Infobase Publishing. p.&#160;299. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780816066735" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 978-0-8160-6673-5</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Facts+on+File+Dictionary+of+Proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Martin+H.+Manser&amp;rft.au=Martin+H.+Manser&amp;rft.date=2007&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B299&amp;rft.pub=Infobase+Publishing&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-8160-6673-5&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DfgaUQc8NbTYC%26pg%3DPA113&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li>
<li>Stone, J. R. (2005). The Routledge Dictionary of Latin Quotations: The Illiterati's Guide to Latin Maxims, Mottoes, Proverbs and Sayings, Routledge. p. 351</li></ul></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="B">B</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latin_proverbs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: B">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><i>Basio saepe volam, cui plagam diligo solam.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Many kiss the hand they wish to cut off.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;1084. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B1084&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Bellum se ipsum alet.</i>
<ul><li>War will feed on itself.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFRoberts2003">Roberts&#32;(2003).&#32;<i>The Age of Liberty: Sweden 1719-1772</i>. Cambridge University Press. p.&#160;19.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Age+of+Liberty%3A+Sweden+1719-1772&amp;rft.aulast=Roberts&amp;rft.au=Roberts&amp;rft.date=2003&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B19&amp;rft.pub=Cambridge+University+Press&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Bene diagnoscitur, bene curatur.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: A disease known is half cured.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMeyer,_Ndura-Ouédraogo2009">Meyer, Ndura-Ouédraogo&#32;(2009).&#32;<i>Seeds of new hope: pan-African peace studies for the 21st century</i>. Africa World Press. p.&#160;331. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/1592216625" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 1592216625</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Seeds+of+new+hope%3A+pan-African+peace+studies+for+the+21st+century&amp;rft.aulast=Meyer%2C+Ndura-Ou%C3%A9draogo&amp;rft.au=Meyer%2C+Ndura-Ou%C3%A9draogo&amp;rft.date=2009&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B331&amp;rft.pub=Africa+World+Press&amp;rft.isbn=1592216625&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Bis dat qui cito dat.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: He gives twice, who gives in a trice.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMawr1885">Mawr, E.B.&#32;(1885).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://editura.mttlc.ro/carti/mawr-analogous-proverbs.pdf">Analogous Proverbs in Ten Languages</a></i>. p.&#160;38.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Analogous+Proverbs+in+Ten+Languages&amp;rft.aulast=Mawr&amp;rft.aufirst=E.B.&amp;rft.au=Mawr%2C+E.B.&amp;rft.date=1885&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B38&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Feditura.mttlc.ro%2Fcarti%2Fmawr-analogous-proverbs.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Brevis oratio penetrat coelos; Longa potatio evacuat scyphos.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Short prayers reach heaven.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMawr1885">Mawr, E.B.&#32;(1885).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://editura.mttlc.ro/carti/mawr-analogous-proverbs.pdf">Analogous Proverbs in Ten Languages</a></i>. p.&#160;75.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Analogous+Proverbs+in+Ten+Languages&amp;rft.aulast=Mawr&amp;rft.aufirst=E.B.&amp;rft.au=Mawr%2C+E.B.&amp;rft.date=1885&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B75&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Feditura.mttlc.ro%2Fcarti%2Fmawr-analogous-proverbs.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="C">C</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latin_proverbs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: C">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><i>Canus honoretur, puer ad documenta citetur.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Gray hairs are honorable.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMawr1885">Mawr, E.B.&#32;(1885).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://editura.mttlc.ro/carti/mawr-analogous-proverbs.pdf">Analogous Proverbs in Ten Languages</a></i>. p.&#160;35.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Analogous+Proverbs+in+Ten+Languages&amp;rft.aulast=Mawr&amp;rft.aufirst=E.B.&amp;rft.au=Mawr%2C+E.B.&amp;rft.date=1885&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B35&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Feditura.mttlc.ro%2Fcarti%2Fmawr-analogous-proverbs.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Carpe diem.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "Seize the day." By <a href="/wiki/Horace" title="Horace">Horace</a>, Odes I,11,8, to <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leuconoe" class="extiw" title="w:Leuconoe">Leuconoe</a>: <i>carpe diem, quam minimum credula postero</i> ("take hold of the day, believing as little as possible in the next").  The verb "carpere" has the literal meaning "to pick, pluck," particularly in reference to the picking of fruits and flowers, and was used figuratively by the Roman poets to mean "to enjoy, use, make use of."</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;765. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B765&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Carthago delenda est.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carthage" class="extiw" title="w:Carthage">Carthage</a> is to be destroyed." Actually, <i>ceterum censeo Carthaginem esse delendam</i> ("Apart from that, I conclude that Carthage must be destroyed") <a href="/wiki/Cato_the_Elder" title="Cato the Elder">Cato the Elder</a> used to end every speech of his to the Senate, on any subject whatsoever, with this phrase. Mentioned to indicate that someone habitually harps on one subject.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Cave ab homine unius libri.</i>
<ul><li>English translation: Fear the man of one <b><a href="/wiki/Book" class="mw-redirect" title="Book">book</a></b>.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;851. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B851&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Cedens in uno cedet in pluribus.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Virtue which parleys is near a surrender.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;957. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B957&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Citius venit malum quam revertitur.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Misfortune comes on horseback and goes away on foot.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;65. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B65&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Cito maturum cito putridum.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Early ripe, early rotten.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;758. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B758&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Cogitationes posteriores sunt saniores.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Second thoughts are best; We shall lose nothing by waiting.</li>
<li>Source for proverb: <cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;747. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B747&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Consilio, quod respuitur, nullum subest auxilium.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: He that will not be counseled cannot be helped.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;964. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B964&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Consuetudinis magna vis est</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Old <b><a href="/wiki/Habit" class="mw-redirect" title="Habit">habits</a></b> die hard.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cicero" title="Cicero">Cicero</a>, <i>Tusculanae Quaestiones</i>, II.37</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Consuetudo altera natura est</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Old habits die hard.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFBreen2010">Breen&#32;(2010).&#32;<i>Imagining an English Reading Public, 1150-1400</i>. Cambridge University Press. p.&#160;46. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0521199220" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0521199220</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Imagining+an+English+Reading+Public%2C+1150-1400&amp;rft.aulast=Breen&amp;rft.au=Breen&amp;rft.date=2010&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B46&amp;rft.pub=Cambridge+University+Press&amp;rft.isbn=0521199220&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Contritium praecedit superbia.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Pride comes before fall.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emmanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European Proverbs, Volym 1</i>. Routledge. p.&#160;1148. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+Proverbs%2C+Volym+1&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emmanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emmanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B1148&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Cor boni concilii statue tecum non est enim tibi aliud pluris illo.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Though thou hast ever so many <b><a href="/wiki/Counsel" class="mw-redirect" title="Counsel">counsel</a></b>lors, yet do not forsake the counsel of thy own soul.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;1044. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B1044&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Corruptissima re publica plurimae leges</i>
<ul><li>Translation: The greater the degeneration of the republic, the more of its laws.</li>
<li>(<a href="/wiki/Tacitus" title="Tacitus">Tacitus</a>) <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Annals_(Tacitus)" class="extiw" title="w:Annals (Tacitus)">Annals</a></i> (117)</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>"Credula est spes improba.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent:  He that lives on hope dances without music.</li>
<li>"Hope is itself a species of happiness, and, perhaps, the chief happiness which this world affords."</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Samuel_Johnson" title="Samuel Johnson">Samuel Johnson</a>, letter of 8 June 1762, in <a href="/wiki/James_Boswell" title="James Boswell">James Boswell</a>, <i>Life of Samuel Johnson</i> (1791), Vol. 1, p. 103</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;952. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B952&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Crede quod habes, et habes.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Fake it till you make it.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFHugh_Moore1831">Hugh Moore&#32;(1831).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=2wb-dMzaXw8C&amp;pg=PA61">A dictionary of quotations from various authors in ancient and modern languages</a></i>. p.&#160;61<span class="reference-accessdate">.&#32;Retrieved on 14 August 2013</span>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=A+dictionary+of+quotations+from+various+authors+in+ancient+and+modern+languages&amp;rft.aulast=Hugh+Moore&amp;rft.au=Hugh+Moore&amp;rft.date=1831&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B61&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3D2wb-dMzaXw8C%26pg%3DPA61&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Cui caput dolet, omnia membra languent.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: When the head is sick, the whole body is sick.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;1117. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B1117&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Cuilibet fatuo placet sua calva.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalentː Every fool is pleased with his own folly.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=86yPOGG3YfcC&amp;pg=PT411">"147"</a>.&#32;<i>Dictionary of European Proverbs</i>. <b>I</b>. Routledge. p.&#160;139. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9781134864607" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 978-1-134-86460-7</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.btitle=147&amp;rft.atitle=Dictionary+of+European+Proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.volume=I&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B139&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-134-86460-7&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3D86yPOGG3YfcC%26pg%3DPT411&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Cuiusvis hominis est errare, nullius nisi insipientis in errore perseverare.</i> 
<ul><li>Any man can make a mistake; only a fool keeps making the same one.</li>
<li>English equivalent: He wrongfully blames the sea who suffers shipwreck twice.</li>
<li>"Papa <a href="/wiki/Georg_Wilhelm_Friedrich_Hegel" title="Georg Wilhelm Friedrich Hegel">Hegel</a> he say that all we learn from history is that we learn nothing from history. <i>I</i> know people who can't even learn from what happened this morning. Hegel must have been taking the long view."</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/John_Brunner" title="John Brunner">John Brunner</a>, <i>Stand on Zanzibar</i> (1968)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cicero" title="Cicero">Marcus Tullius Cicero</a>, Philippica XII, ii, 5</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Curae canitiem inducunt.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Fretting cares make grey hairs.</li>
<li>Source for proverb: <cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;631. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B631&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Custode et cura natura potentior omni.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Nature is beyond all teaching.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;764. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B764&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>

</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="D">D</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latin_proverbs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: D">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><i><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/de_gustibus_non_est_disputandum" class="extiw" title="wikt:de gustibus non est disputandum">De gustibus non est disputandum</a>.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: There is no disputing about tastes.</li>
<li>English equivalent: There is no accounting for taste.</li>
<li>Alternative form:</li></ul></li>
<li><i><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/de_gustibus_et_coloribus_non_est_disputandum" class="extiw" title="wikt:de gustibus et coloribus non est disputandum">De gustibus et coloribus non est disputandum</a>.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "There's no arguing about tastes and colors."</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book"><i>De Gustibus Non Est Disputandum: Dramma Giocoso Per Musica Da Rappresentarsi In Monaco Di Baviera</i>. Vötter. 1759.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=De+Gustibus+Non+Est+Disputandum%3A+Dramma+Giocoso+Per+Musica+Da+Rappresentarsi+In+Monaco+Di+Baviera&amp;rft.date=1759&amp;rft.pub=V%C3%B6tter&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFH._Z_Riley1866">H. Z Riley&#32;(1866).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=B3y1enBOD9kC&amp;pg=PA73">Dictionary of Latin Quotations Proverbs Maximus and Mottos, Classical and Medieval, Including Law Terms and Phrases</a></i>. Bell &amp; Daldy. p.&#160;73.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+Latin+Quotations+Proverbs+Maximus+and+Mottos%2C+Classical+and+Medieval%2C+Including+Law+Terms+and+Phrases&amp;rft.aulast=H.+Z+Riley&amp;rft.au=H.+Z+Riley&amp;rft.date=1866&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B73&amp;rft.pub=Bell+%26+Daldy&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DB3y1enBOD9kC%26pg%3DPA73&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Deus quem punire vult dementat.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Whom God will destroy, he first make mad.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;841. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B841&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Diem vesper commendat.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: Celebrate the day when it is evening.</li>
<li>Meaning: Don't celebrate until you are 100% sure there is a reason to do so.; Don't count your chickens before they're hatched.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1998">Strauss, Emmanuel&#32;(1998).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European Proverbs</i>. Routledge. p.&#160;200. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415160502" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415160502</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+Proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emmanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emmanuel&amp;rft.date=1998&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B200&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415160502&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Difficile est longum subito deponere amorem.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: True love never grows old.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;1107. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B1107&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Dii facientes adiuvant.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: Gods help those who do.</li>
<li>English equivalent: God helps them that help themselves.</li>
<li>Meaning: "When in trouble first of all every one himself should do his best to improve his condition."</li>
<li>Source for meaning of English equivalent: <cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFPaczolay1997">Paczolay, Gyula&#32;(1997).&#32;<i>European Proverbs in 55 languages</i>. DeProverbio.com. p.&#160;150. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/1875943447" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 1-875943-44-7</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=European+Proverbs+in+55+languages&amp;rft.aulast=Paczolay&amp;rft.aufirst=Gyula&amp;rft.au=Paczolay%2C+Gyula&amp;rft.date=1997&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B150&amp;rft.pub=DeProverbio.com&amp;rft.isbn=1-875943-44-7&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFCantera_Ortiz_de_Urbina2005">Cantera Ortiz de Urbina, Jesús&#32;(16 November 2005).&#32;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=xll5lkkwNI0C&amp;pg=PA83">"975"</a>.&#32;<i>Refranero latino</i>. Ediciones Akal. p.&#160;83. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9788446012962" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 978-84-460-1296-2</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.btitle=975&amp;rft.atitle=Refranero+latino&amp;rft.aulast=Cantera+Ortiz+de+Urbina&amp;rft.aufirst=Jes%C3%BAs&amp;rft.au=Cantera+Ortiz+de+Urbina%2C+Jes%C3%BAs&amp;rft.date=16+November+2005&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B83&amp;rft.pub=Ediciones+Akal&amp;rft.isbn=978-84-460-1296-2&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3Dxll5lkkwNI0C%26pg%3DPA83&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Dives aut iniquus est, aut iniqui heres.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: No one gets rich quickly if he is honest.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;963. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B963&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Dives est qui sibi nihil deesse putat.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: The rich man is the one who thinks to himself that nothing was lacking.</li>
<li>Note: Another way to phrase this is by this quote:
<ul><li>No one – not a single person out of a thousand [elderly interviewed because of their wisdom expertise] – said that to be happy you should try and work as hard as you can to make money to buy the things you want.</li>
<li>No one – not a single person –– said it's important to be at least as wealthy as the people around you, and if you have more than they do it's real success.</li>
<li>No one – not a single person –– said you should choose your work based on your desired future earning power.”</li></ul></li>
<li>From: <cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFBrody2011">Brody, Jane&#32;(2011).&#32;<i>30 Lessons for Living</i>. Penguin Group. p.&#160;57. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/1594630844" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 1594630844</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=30+Lessons+for+Living&amp;rft.aulast=Brody&amp;rft.aufirst=Jane&amp;rft.au=Brody%2C+Jane&amp;rft.date=2011&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B57&amp;rft.pub=Penguin+Group&amp;rft.isbn=1594630844&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li>
<li>English equivalent: Wealth rarely brings happiness.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;670. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B670&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Divide et impera.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: Divide and govern [or conquer].  Attributed to <a href="/wiki/Julius_Caesar" title="Julius Caesar">Julius Caesar</a>.</li>
<li>English equivalent: Divide and conquer.</li>
<li>Meaning: "The best way to conquer or control a group of people is by encouraging them to fight among themselves rather than allowing them to unite in opposition to the ruling authority."</li>
<li>Source for meaning of English equivalent: <cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMartin_H._Manser2007">Martin H. Manser&#32;(2007).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=fgaUQc8NbTYC&amp;pg=PA57">The Facts on File Dictionary of Proverbs</a></i>. Infobase Publishing. p.&#160;57. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780816066735" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 978-0-8160-6673-5</a><span class="reference-accessdate">.&#32;Retrieved on 13 August 2013</span>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Facts+on+File+Dictionary+of+Proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Martin+H.+Manser&amp;rft.au=Martin+H.+Manser&amp;rft.date=2007&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B57&amp;rft.pub=Infobase+Publishing&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-8160-6673-5&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DfgaUQc8NbTYC%26pg%3DPA57&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=sm96Wlt8Ql0C&amp;pg=PT565">"823"</a>.&#32;<i>Concise Dictionary of European Proverbs</i>. <ul><li>English equivalent: Good riding at two anchors, men have told, for if the one fails, the other may hold.</li>

<ul><li><i>Ductus Exemplo</i>
<ul><li>Translation: Lead by Example.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFGray2009">Gray&#32;(2009).&#32;<i>Embedded: a Marine Corps adviser inside the Iraqi army</i>. Naval Institute Press. p.&#160;74. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/1591143403" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 1591143403</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Embedded%3A+a+Marine+Corps+adviser+inside+the+Iraqi+army&amp;rft.aulast=Gray&amp;rft.au=Gray&amp;rft.date=2009&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B74&amp;rft.pub=Naval+Institute+Press&amp;rft.isbn=1591143403&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Dulce et decorum est pro patria mori.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: It is sweet and honorable to die for the fatherland. By <a href="/wiki/Horace" title="Horace">Horace</a>, <i>Odes</i> III, 2, 13, frequently quoted on war memorials, and notably in the poem <i>Dulce Et Decorum Est</i> by <a href="/wiki/Wilfred_Owen" title="Wilfred Owen">Wilfred Owen</a>, who calls it "the old lie".</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Dulce pomum quum abest custos.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: Sweet is the apple when the keeper is away.</li>
<li>English equivalent: Forbidden fruit is sweetest.</li>
<li>Meaning: "Things that you must not have or do are always the most desirable."</li>
<li>Source for meaning of English equivalent: <cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMartin_H._Manser2007">Martin H. Manser&#32;(2007).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=fgaUQc8NbTYC&amp;pg=PA93">The Facts on File Dictionary of Proverbs</a></i>. <li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFJános_Erdélyi1851">János Erdélyi&#32;(1851).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=uqwOAAAAQAAJ&amp;pg=PA169">Magyar közmondások könlyve</a></i>. <ul><li><i>Dulcior illa sapit caro, quae magis ossibus haeret.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: The sweetest flesh is near the bones.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;"1666".&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>. <b>II</b>. Routledge. p.&#160;1176. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.btitle=1666&amp;rft.atitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.volume=II&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B1176&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Dum canem caedimus, corrosisse dicitur corrium.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: If you want to beat a dog you will easily find a stick.</li>
<li>Meaning: Someone who wants to be mean will find things to be mean about no matter what.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1998">Strauss, Emmanuel&#32;(1998).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European Proverbs</i>. Routledge. p.&#160;104. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415160502" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415160502</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+Proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emmanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emmanuel&amp;rft.date=1998&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B104&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415160502&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Dum satur est venter, gaudet caput inde libenter.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: When the belly is full, the head is pleased.</li>
<li>English equivalent: Full stomach, contented heart.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFCantera_Ortiz_de_Urbina2005">Cantera Ortiz de Urbina, Jesús&#32;(16 November 2005).&#32;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=xll5lkkwNI0C&amp;pg=PA69">"768"</a>.&#32;<i>Refranero latino</i>. Ediciones Akal. p.&#160;68. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9788446012962" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 978-84-460-1296-2</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.btitle=768&amp;rft.atitle=Refranero+latino&amp;rft.aulast=Cantera+Ortiz+de+Urbina&amp;rft.aufirst=Jes%C3%BAs&amp;rft.au=Cantera+Ortiz+de+Urbina%2C+Jes%C3%BAs&amp;rft.date=16+November+2005&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B68&amp;rft.pub=Ediciones+Akal&amp;rft.isbn=978-84-460-1296-2&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3Dxll5lkkwNI0C%26pg%3DPA69&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Dum spiro, spero.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "As long as I breathe, I hope." Translated as "While I breathe, I hope" the motto of the State of South Carolina [<a class="external autonumber" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Carolina">[1]</a>]</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFGunter2000">Gunter&#32;(2000).&#32;<i>Dum Spiro, Spero: While I Breathe, I Hope</i>. In His Steps Publishing. pp.&#160;180. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/1585350192" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 1585350192</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dum+Spiro%2C+Spero%3A+While+I+Breathe%2C+I+Hope&amp;rft.aulast=Gunter&amp;rft.au=Gunter&amp;rft.date=2000&amp;rft.pages=pp.%26nbsp%3B180&amp;rft.pub=In+His+Steps+Publishing&amp;rft.isbn=1585350192&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li>
<li>English equivalent: As long as there is life there is hope.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Dum vivimus, vivamus!</i>
<ul><li>Translation: While we live, let us live!</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFOrganization)1972">Organization)&#32;(1972).&#32;<i>Dum Vivimus, Vivamus: A Chronicle of the First Century of the Knights of Momus, 1872-1972</i>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dum+Vivimus%2C+Vivamus%3A+A+Chronicle+of+the+First+Century+of+the+Knights+of+Momus%2C+1872-1972&amp;rft.aulast=Organization%29&amp;rft.au=Organization%29&amp;rft.date=1972&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Dum vita est, spes est.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: While there is life, there is hope.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFBretzke1998">Bretzke&#32;(1998).&#32;<i>Consecrated Phrases: A Latin Theological Dictionary&#160;: Latin Expressions Commonly Found in Theological Writings</i>. Liturgical Press. p.&#160;41. ISBN 1.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Consecrated+Phrases%3A+A+Latin+Theological+Dictionary+%3A+Latin+Expressions+Commonly+Found+in+Theological+Writings&amp;rft.aulast=Bretzke&amp;rft.au=Bretzke&amp;rft.date=1998&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B41&amp;rft.pub=Liturgical+Press&amp;rft.isbn=1&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="E">E</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latin_proverbs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: E">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><i>Ecce omnis, qui dicit vulgo proverbium, in te assumet illud dicens: Sicut mater, ita et filia ejus.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: Behold, every one that useth a common proverb, shall use this against thee, saying, As is the mother, so is her daughter.</li>
<li>English equivalent: Like mother, like daughter.</li>
<li>Meaning: "Daughters may look and behave like their mothers. This is due to inheritance and the example observed closely and daily."</li>
<li>Source for meaning and proverbs: <cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFPaczolay1997">Paczolay, Gyula&#32;(1997).&#32;<i>European Proverbs in 55 languages</i>. DeProverbio.com. p.&#160;137. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/1875943447" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 1-875943-44-7</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=European+Proverbs+in+55+languages&amp;rft.aulast=Paczolay&amp;rft.aufirst=Gyula&amp;rft.au=Paczolay%2C+Gyula&amp;rft.date=1997&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B137&amp;rft.pub=DeProverbio.com&amp;rft.isbn=1-875943-44-7&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Effectus sequitir causam.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: Effect follows a reason.</li>
<li>English equivalent: Every why has a wherefore.</li>
<li>Meaning: "Everything has an underlying reason."</li>
<li>Source for meaning of English equivalent: <cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMartin_H._Manser2007">Martin H. Manser&#32;(2007).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=fgaUQc8NbTYC&amp;pg=PA80">The Facts on File Dictionary of Proverbs</a></i>. Infobase Publishing. p.&#160;80. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780816066735" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 978-0-8160-6673-5</a><span class="reference-accessdate">.&#32;Retrieved on 22 September 2013</span>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Facts+on+File+Dictionary+of+Proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Martin+H.+Manser&amp;rft.au=Martin+H.+Manser&amp;rft.date=2007&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B80&amp;rft.pub=Infobase+Publishing&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-8160-6673-5&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DfgaUQc8NbTYC%26pg%3DPA80&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;765. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B765&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Eodem cubito, eadem trutina, pari libra.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: The elbow, the same balance, an equal balance.</li>
<li>English equivalent: Whatever measure you deal out to others will be dealt back to you.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;1219. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B1219&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Ex granis fit acervus.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: A heap is made from grains.</li>
<li>English equivalent: Every little helps.</li>
<li>Meaning: "All contributions, however small, are of use."</li>
<li>Source for meaning of English equivalent: <cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMartin_H._Manser2007">Martin H. Manser&#32;(2007).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=fgaUQc8NbTYC&amp;pg=PA78">The Facts on File Dictionary of Proverbs</a></i>. Infobase Publishing. p.&#160;77. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780816066735" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 978-0-8160-6673-5</a><span class="reference-accessdate">.&#32;Retrieved on 20 September 2013</span>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Facts+on+File+Dictionary+of+Proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Martin+H.+Manser&amp;rft.au=Martin+H.+Manser&amp;rft.date=2007&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B77&amp;rft.pub=Infobase+Publishing&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-8160-6673-5&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DfgaUQc8NbTYC%26pg%3DPA78&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li>
<li>Source for proverbs: <cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMawr1885">Mawr, E.B.&#32;(1885).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://editura.mttlc.ro/carti/mawr-analogous-proverbs.pdf">Analogous Proverbs in Ten Languages</a></i>. p.&#160;26.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Analogous+Proverbs+in+Ten+Languages&amp;rft.aulast=Mawr&amp;rft.aufirst=E.B.&amp;rft.au=Mawr%2C+E.B.&amp;rft.date=1885&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B26&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Feditura.mttlc.ro%2Fcarti%2Fmawr-analogous-proverbs.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Et ipsa scientia potestas est.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "And knowledge itself, is power" (<a href="/wiki/Francis_Bacon" title="Francis Bacon">Francis Bacon</a>, <i>Meditationes sacrae</i>)</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFDjité2008">Djité&#32;(2008).&#32;<i>The Sociolinguistics of Development in Africa</i>. Multilingual Matters. p.&#160;53. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/1847690459" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 1847690459</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Sociolinguistics+of+Development+in+Africa&amp;rft.aulast=Djit%C3%A9&amp;rft.au=Djit%C3%A9&amp;rft.date=2008&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B53&amp;rft.pub=Multilingual+Matters&amp;rft.isbn=1847690459&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Ex malis moribus bonae leges natae sunt.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: Bad customs have given birth to good laws.</li>
<li>English equivalent: Good laws have sprung from bad customs.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;879. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B879&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Ex nihilo nihil fit.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "Nothing comes from nothing" (you need to work for something; also the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conservation_law" class="extiw" title="w:Conservation law">Conservation Law</a> in philosophy and modern science) (<a href="/wiki/Lucretius" title="Lucretius">Lucretius</a>). This is also a famous Shakespeare quote in <a href="/wiki/King_Lear" title="King Lear">King Lear</a>.</li>
