<li>"If you would have any thing done for you, you must give something, for people will not serve you for nothing."</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFJames_Kelly1818">James Kelly&#32;(1818).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=tsBCAAAAcAAJ&amp;pg=GBS.PA13">A Complete Collection of Scottish Proverbs Explained and Made Intelligible to the English Reader</a></i>. Rodwell and Martin. p.&#160;13.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=A+Complete+Collection+of+Scottish+Proverbs+Explained+and+Made+Intelligible+to+the+English+Reader&amp;rft.aulast=James+Kelly&amp;rft.au=James+Kelly&amp;rft.date=1818&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B13&amp;rft.pub=Rodwell+and+Martin&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DtsBCAAAAcAAJ%26pg%3DGBS.PA13&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFCampbell,_O&#39;Rourke,_Silverstein2007">Campbell, O'Rourke, Silverstein&#32;(2007).&#32;<i>Causation and Explanation</i>. Mit Press. p.&#160;291. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0262033631" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0262033631</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Causation+and+Explanation&amp;rft.aulast=Campbell%2C+O%27Rourke%2C+Silverstein&amp;rft.au=Campbell%2C+O%27Rourke%2C+Silverstein&amp;rft.date=2007&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B291&amp;rft.pub=Mit+Press&amp;rft.isbn=0262033631&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Exceptio probat regulam in casibus non exceptis</i>.
<ul><li>Translation: "The exception confirms the rule in cases not excepted" (<a href="/wiki/Cicero" title="Cicero">Cicero</a>, <i>Pro Balbo</i>)</li>
<li>Meaning: If an exception to a rule is explicitly stated (such as a "no right turns on red light" sign at an intersection), that allows one to conclude the general rule to which this is an exception (i.e. "right turns are permitted on red lights unless a sign says otherwise").</li>
<li>English equivalent: "The <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/exception_proves_the_rule" class="extiw" title="w:exception proves the rule">exception proves the rule</a>" (though this is often used in other senses).</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Excusatio non petita, accusatio manifesta.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: A guilty conscience needs no accuser.</li>
<li>Meaning: "People who know they have done wrong reveal their guilt by the things they say or the way they interpret what other people say."</li>
<li>Source for meaning of English equivalent: <cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMartin_H._Manser2007">Martin H. Manser&#32;(2007).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=fgaUQc8NbTYC&amp;pg=PA112">The Facts on File Dictionary of Proverbs</a></i>. Infobase Publishing. p.&#160;112. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780816066735" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 978-0-8160-6673-5</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Facts+on+File+Dictionary+of+Proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Martin+H.+Manser&amp;rft.au=Martin+H.+Manser&amp;rft.date=2007&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B112&amp;rft.pub=Infobase+Publishing&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-8160-6673-5&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DfgaUQc8NbTYC%26pg%3DPA112&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=sm96Wlt8Ql0C&amp;pg=PT565">"243"</a>.&#32;<i>Concise Dictionary of European Proverbs</i>. Routledge. p.&#160;227. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9781136789786" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 978-1-136-78978-6</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.btitle=243&amp;rft.atitle=Concise+Dictionary+of+European+Proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B227&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-136-78978-6&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3Dsm96Wlt8Ql0C%26pg%3DPT565&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Extremis malis extrema remedia.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: Extreme remedies for extreme ills.</li>
<li>English equivalent: Desperate diseases must have desperate remedies.</li>
<li>Meaning: "Drastic action is called for – and justified – when you find yourself in a particularly difficult situation."</li>
<li>Source for meaning: <cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMartin_H._Manser2007">Martin H. Manser&#32;(2007).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=fgaUQc8NbTYC&amp;pg=PA53">The Facts on File Dictionary of Proverbs</a></i>. Infobase Publishing. p.&#160;53. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780816066735" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 978-0-8160-6673-5</a><span class="reference-accessdate">.&#32;Retrieved on 10 August 2013</span>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Facts+on+File+Dictionary+of+Proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Martin+H.+Manser&amp;rft.au=Martin+H.+Manser&amp;rft.date=2007&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B53&amp;rft.pub=Infobase+Publishing&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-8160-6673-5&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DfgaUQc8NbTYC%26pg%3DPA53&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;688. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B688&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Expecta bos olim herba.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: Waiting for the grass the cow dies.</li>
<li>English equivalent: While the grass grows the steed starves.</li>
<li>Meaning: Dreams or expectations may be realized too late.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;1228. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B1228&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="F">F</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latin_proverbs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: F">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><i>Facilis descensus Averni.</i>
<ul><li>The descent into hell is easy.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMawr1885">Mawr, E.B.&#32;(1885).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://editura.mttlc.ro/carti/mawr-analogous-proverbs.pdf">Analogous Proverbs in Ten Languages</a></i>. p.&#160;39.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Analogous+Proverbs+in+Ten+Languages&amp;rft.aulast=Mawr&amp;rft.aufirst=E.B.&amp;rft.au=Mawr%2C+E.B.&amp;rft.date=1885&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B39&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Feditura.mttlc.ro%2Fcarti%2Fmawr-analogous-proverbs.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Factis ut credam facis.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: No need of words, trust deeds.</li>
<li>Meaning: Actions may be, and indeed sometimes are deceptive in a measure though not as much so as words; and accordingly are received in general as more full and satisfactory proofs of the real disposition and character of persons than verbal expressions.</li>
<li>Source for meaning:<cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFPorter1845">Porter, William Henry&#32;(1845).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=KA4oAAAAYAAJ&amp;pg=PA10">Proverbs: Arranged in Alphabetical Order ...</a></i>. Munroe and Company. p.&#160;10.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Proverbs%3A+Arranged+in+Alphabetical+Order+...&amp;rft.aulast=Porter&amp;rft.aufirst=William+Henry&amp;rft.au=Porter%2C+William+Henry&amp;rft.date=1845&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B10&amp;rft.pub=Munroe+and+Company&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DKA4oAAAAYAAJ%26pg%3DPA10&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;91. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B91&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Festina lente!</i>
<ul><li>Translation: Make haste slowly.</li>
<li>English equivalent: More speed less haste.</li>
<li>English meaning: proceed quickly but with caution, a motto of <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Aurelius" title="Marcus Aurelius">Marcus Aurelius</a></li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFRochester_Institute_of_Technology1980">Rochester Institute of Technology&#32;(1980).&#32;<i>Festina lente</i>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Festina+lente&amp;rft.aulast=Rochester+Institute+of+Technology&amp;rft.au=Rochester+Institute+of+Technology&amp;rft.date=1980&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Fides facit fidem.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Confidence begets confidence.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;187. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B187&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Fidite Nemini</i>
<ul><li>Translation: Trust no one.</li>
<li>Cinderella, <i>The More Things Change</i> (1991)</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book"><i>Conciones Adventuales: De De Captivitate Petri, Figurante Captivitatem Peccatoris</i>. Verdussen. 1737. p.&#160;113.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Conciones+Adventuales%3A+De+De+Captivitate+Petri%2C+Figurante+Captivitatem+Peccatoris&amp;rft.date=1737&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B113&amp;rft.pub=Verdussen&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Finis origine pendet.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: The end hangs on the beginning.</li>
<li>English equivalent: Such a beginning, such an end.</li>
<li>Meaning: The outcome of things depends on how they start.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Forma bonum fragile est.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: All that is fair must fade.</li>
<li>English meaning: Nothing lasts forever.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMartin_H._Manser2007">Martin H. Manser&#32;(2007).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=fgaUQc8NbTYC&amp;pg=PA80">The Facts on File Dictionary of Proverbs</a></i>. Infobase Publishing. p.&#160;80. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780816066735" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 978-0-8160-6673-5</a><span class="reference-accessdate">.&#32;Retrieved on 21 September 2013</span>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Facts+on+File+Dictionary+of+Proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Martin+H.+Manser&amp;rft.au=Martin+H.+Manser&amp;rft.date=2007&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B80&amp;rft.pub=Infobase+Publishing&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-8160-6673-5&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DfgaUQc8NbTYC%26pg%3DPA80&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMawr1885">Mawr, E.B.&#32;(1885).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://editura.mttlc.ro/carti/mawr-analogous-proverbs.pdf">Analogous Proverbs in Ten Languages</a></i>. p.&#160;10.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Analogous+Proverbs+in+Ten+Languages&amp;rft.aulast=Mawr&amp;rft.aufirst=E.B.&amp;rft.au=Mawr%2C+E.B.&amp;rft.date=1885&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B10&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Feditura.mttlc.ro%2Fcarti%2Fmawr-analogous-proverbs.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Fortes fortuna iuvat</i>
<ul><li>Translation: Fortune favors the brave. (cf. <i>Audaces fortuna iuvat</i>.) (<a href="/wiki/Terence" title="Terence">Terence</a>)</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMarchesi2008">Marchesi&#32;(2008).&#32;<i>The Art of Pliny's Letters: A Poetics of Allusion in the Private Correspondence</i>. Cambridge University Press. p.&#160;176. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0521882273" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0521882273</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Art+of+Pliny%27s+Letters%3A+A+Poetics+of+Allusion+in+the+Private+Correspondence&amp;rft.aulast=Marchesi&amp;rft.au=Marchesi&amp;rft.date=2008&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B176&amp;rft.pub=Cambridge+University+Press&amp;rft.isbn=0521882273&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Fraus hominum ad perniciem, et integritas ad salutem vocat.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Honesty is the best policy.</li>
<li>Meaning: Being honest or telling the truth is always the wisest course of action.</li>
<li>Source for meaning of English equivalent: <cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMartin_H._Manser2007">Martin H. Manser&#32;(2007).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=fgaUQc8NbTYC&amp;pg=PA128">The Facts on File Dictionary of Proverbs</a></i>. Infobase Publishing. p.&#160;128. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780816066735" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 978-0-8160-6673-5</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Facts+on+File+Dictionary+of+Proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Martin+H.+Manser&amp;rft.au=Martin+H.+Manser&amp;rft.date=2007&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B128&amp;rft.pub=Infobase+Publishing&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-8160-6673-5&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DfgaUQc8NbTYC%26pg%3DPA128&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMawr1885">Mawr, E.B.&#32;(1885).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://editura.mttlc.ro/carti/mawr-analogous-proverbs.pdf">Analogous Proverbs in Ten Languages</a></i>. p.&#160;X.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Analogous+Proverbs+in+Ten+Languages&amp;rft.aulast=Mawr&amp;rft.aufirst=E.B.&amp;rft.au=Mawr%2C+E.B.&amp;rft.date=1885&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3BX&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Feditura.mttlc.ro%2Fcarti%2Fmawr-analogous-proverbs.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Fronti nulla fides.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Appearances deceive.</li>
<li>Source: <cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1998">Strauss, Emmanuel&#32;(1998).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European Proverbs</i>. Routledge. p.&#160;124. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415160502" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415160502</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+Proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emmanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emmanuel&amp;rft.date=1998&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B124&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415160502&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="G">G</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latin_proverbs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: G">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><i>Generosus equus non curat canem latrantem</i>.
<ul><li>English equivalent: The dogs bark but the caravan passes on.</li>
<li>"Everyone's got opinions, but nobody's got the answers" so let the world say what it will.</li>
<li>Thomas Carl Keifer, <i>Somebody Save Me</i> (1987)</li>
<li>Source: <cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1998">Strauss, Emmanuel&#32;(1998).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European Proverbs</i>. Routledge. p.&#160;340. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415160502" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415160502</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+Proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emmanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emmanuel&amp;rft.date=1998&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B340&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415160502&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Gloriosum est iniurias oblivisci.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Forgive and forget.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFRauschen,_Geyer,_Albers,_Zellinger1933">Rauschen, Geyer, Albers, Zellinger&#32;(1933).&#32;<i>Florilegium patristicum</i>. P. Hanstein. p.&#160;58.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Florilegium+patristicum&amp;rft.aulast=Rauschen%2C+Geyer%2C+Albers%2C+Zellinger&amp;rft.au=Rauschen%2C+Geyer%2C+Albers%2C+Zellinger&amp;rft.date=1933&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B58&amp;rft.pub=P.+Hanstein&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Gutta cavat lapidem</i>
<ul><li>A drop hollows out the stone. (<a href="/wiki/Ovid" title="Ovid">Ovid</a>, <i>Epistles</i>)</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Gutta cavat lapidem non bis, sed saepe cadendo; sic homo fit sapiens non bis, sed saepe legendo.</i>
<ul><li>A drop hollows out the stone by falling not twice, but many times; so too is a person made wise by reading not two, but many <b><a href="/wiki/Book" class="mw-redirect" title="Book">book</a></b>s.</li>
<li>(<a href="/wiki/Giordano_Bruno" title="Giordano Bruno">Giordano Bruno</a>, <i>Il Candelaio</i>)</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Gutta cavat lapidem non vi, sed saepe cadendo</i>
<ul><li>A drop hollows out the stone not by force, but falling many times. (original latin proverb).</li></ul></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="H">H</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latin_proverbs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: H">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><i>Historia est vitae magistra.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "History is the tutor of life.”</li>
<li>Dover, R. and M. S. Goodman Learning from the Secret Past: Cases in British Intelligence History, Georgetown University Press.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Hodie mihi, cras tibi.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "What's to me today, tomorrow to you.”</li>
<li>English equivalent: The door swings both ways; What goes around comes around.</li>
<li>Ferler, J. (1723). Hodie Mihi, Cras Tibi, Gruber.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Hodie mihi, eras tibi.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Each dog has his day.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMawr1885">Mawr, E.B.&#32;(1885).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://editura.mttlc.ro/carti/mawr-analogous-proverbs.pdf">Analogous Proverbs in Ten Languages</a></i>. p.&#160;22.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Analogous+Proverbs+in+Ten+Languages&amp;rft.aulast=Mawr&amp;rft.aufirst=E.B.&amp;rft.au=Mawr%2C+E.B.&amp;rft.date=1885&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B22&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Feditura.mttlc.ro%2Fcarti%2Fmawr-analogous-proverbs.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Homines quod volunt credunt.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "Men believe what they want to." (<a href="/wiki/Julius_Caesar" title="Julius Caesar">Julius Caesar</a>)</li>
<li>Lautenbach, E. (2002). Latein-Deutsch: Zitaten-Lexikon: Quellennachweise, Lit.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Homo cogitat, Deus iudicat.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: Man proposes but God disposes.</li>
<li>Meaning: Things often don't turn out as you have planned.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1998">Strauss, Emmanuel&#32;(1998).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European Proverbs</i>. Routledge. p.&#160;103. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415160502" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415160502</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+Proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emmanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emmanuel&amp;rft.date=1998&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B103&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415160502&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Honor sequitir fugientem.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: Honor follows the fleeing.</li>
<li>English equivalent: Follow glory and it will flee, flee glory and it will follow thee.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;832. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B832&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Hortamur fari, quo sanguine cretus.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Good blood always shows itself.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMawr1885">Mawr, E.B.&#32;(1885).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://editura.mttlc.ro/carti/mawr-analogous-proverbs.pdf">Analogous Proverbs in Ten Languages</a></i>. p.&#160;34.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Analogous+Proverbs+in+Ten+Languages&amp;rft.aulast=Mawr&amp;rft.aufirst=E.B.&amp;rft.au=Mawr%2C+E.B.&amp;rft.date=1885&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B34&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Feditura.mttlc.ro%2Fcarti%2Fmawr-analogous-proverbs.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Hostium munera, non munera.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: Gifts of enemies are no gifts.</li>
<li>Note: "This advice has its root in the story of the Trojan Horse, the treacherous subterfuge by which the Greeks finally overcame their trojan adversaries at the end of the Trojan War."</li>
<li>English equivalent: Beware of Greeks bearing gifts.</li>
<li>Meaning: "Do not trust gifts or favors if they come from an enemy."</li>
<li>Source for meaning: <cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMartin_H._ManserDavid_H._Pickering2003">Martin H. Manser; David H. Pickering&#32;(2003).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=LIcL56NQ3gsC&amp;pg=PA46">The Facts On File Dictionary of Classical and Biblical Allusions</a></i>. Infobase Publishing. p.&#160;46. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780816048687" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 978-0-8160-4868-7</a><span class="reference-accessdate">.&#32;Retrieved on 1 July 2013</span>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Facts+On+File+Dictionary+of+Classical+and+Biblical+Allusions&amp;rft.aulast=Martin+H.+Manser&amp;rft.au=Martin+H.+Manser&amp;rft.au=David+H.+Pickering&amp;rft.date=2003&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B46&amp;rft.pub=Infobase+Publishing&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-8160-4868-7&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DLIcL56NQ3gsC%26pg%3DPA46&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;855. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B855&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="I">I</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latin_proverbs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: I">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Note: I and J are the same letter in Latin.
</p>
<ul><li><i>Ignavum fortuna repugnat.</i>
<ul><li>Fortune disdains the lazy.</li>
<li>"Don't yield to that alluring witch, laziness, or else be prepared to surrender all that you have won in your better moments."</li>
<li>Horace, Satires</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;601. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B601&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Ignorantia legis non excusat</i>
<ul><li>Translation: Ignorance of the law is no excuse.</li>
<li>Source: <cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1998">Strauss, Emmanuel&#32;(1998).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European Proverbs</i>. Routledge. p.&#160;287. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415160502" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415160502</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+Proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emmanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emmanuel&amp;rft.date=1998&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B287&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415160502&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Imperare sibi maximum imperium est.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: To rule yourself is the ultimate power. (<a href="/wiki/Seneca_the_Younger" title="Seneca the Younger">Seneca</a>)</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emmanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European Proverbs, Volym 1</i>. Routledge. p.&#160;915. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+Proverbs%2C+Volym+1&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emmanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emmanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B915&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Improbe Neptunum accusat, qui iterum naufragiam facit.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: He complains wrongfully at the sea that suffer shipwreck twice.</li>
<li>Meaning: Don't do the same thing again and expect different results.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;898. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B898&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>In dubio, abstine.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: When in doubt, abstain.</li>
<li>English equivalent: When in doubt, leave it out.</li>
<li>Meaning: "If you are unsure what to do, it is best to do nothing at all."</li>
<li>Source for meaning of English equivalent: <cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMartin_H._Manser2007">Martin H. Manser&#32;(2007).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=fgaUQc8NbTYC&amp;pg=PA123">The Facts on File Dictionary of Proverbs</a></i>. Infobase Publishing. p.&#160;296. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780816066735" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 978-0-8160-6673-5</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Facts+on+File+Dictionary+of+Proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Martin+H.+Manser&amp;rft.au=Martin+H.+Manser&amp;rft.date=2007&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B296&amp;rft.pub=Infobase+Publishing&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-8160-6673-5&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DfgaUQc8NbTYC%26pg%3DPA123&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;1223. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B1223&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>In dubio pro reo.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "When in doubt, in favour of the accused". (<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Corpus_Juris_Civilis" class="extiw" title="w:Corpus Juris Civilis">Corpus Juris Civilis</a>)</li>
<li>Stree, W. (1962). In dubio pro reo, Mohr.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>In iudicando criminosa est celeritas.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: Hasty judgments are criminal.</li>
<li>English equivalent: Hasty judgment leads to repentance.</li>
<li>Meaning: A quick evaluation is a terrible evaluation.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;196. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B196&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>In necessariis unitas, in dubiis libertas, in omnibus caritas</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "In necessary things unity, in doubtful things liberty, in all things charity" (often misattributed to <a href="/wiki/Augustine_of_Hippo" title="Augustine of Hippo">St Augustine</a>).</li>
<li>Bretzke, J. T. (1998). Consecrated Phrases: A Latin Theological Dictionary&#160;: Latin Expressions Commonly Found in Theological Writings, Liturgical Press.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>In nullum avarus bonus est, in se pessimus.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: The covetous man is good to none and worst to himself.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;83. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B83&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>In propria causa nemo debet esse iudex.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: No one should be the judge in his own trial.</li>
<li>English equivalent: No one can be the judge in his own case.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;1038. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B1038&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>In risu agnoscitur fatuus.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: A fool is ever laughing.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFEmanuel_Strauss1994">Emanuel Strauss&#32;(1994).&#32;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=sm96Wlt8Ql0C&amp;pg=PT102">"137"</a>.&#32;<i>Concise Dictionary of European Proverbs</i>. Routledge. p.&#160;102. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9781136789786" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 978-1-136-78978-6</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.btitle=137&amp;rft.atitle=Concise+Dictionary+of+European+Proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Emanuel+Strauss&amp;rft.au=Emanuel+Strauss&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B102&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-136-78978-6&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3Dsm96Wlt8Ql0C%26pg%3DPT102&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>In vino veritas.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: There is truth in vine.</li>
<li>English equivalent: In wine there is truth.</li>
<li>Meaning: Alcohol consumed removes the inhibition against telling the truth that occasionally one would like to keep secret.</li>
<li>Source for meaning and proverbs: <cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFPaczolay1997">Paczolay, Gyula&#32;(1997).&#32;<i>European Proverbs in 55 languages</i>. DeProverbio.com. p.&#160;272. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/1875943447" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 1-875943-44-7</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=European+Proverbs+in+55+languages&amp;rft.aulast=Paczolay&amp;rft.aufirst=Gyula&amp;rft.au=Paczolay%2C+Gyula&amp;rft.date=1997&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B272&amp;rft.pub=DeProverbio.com&amp;rft.isbn=1-875943-44-7&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Inimicum quamvis humilem docti est metuere.</i>
<ul><li>Idiomatic and literal translation: There is no little enemy.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;718. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B718&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li>
<li>Literal translation: The wise man must fear a humble enemy.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Innumeras curas secum adferunt liberi.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: Children bring with them countless cares.</li>
<li>English equivalent: Children are uncertain comforts but certain cares.</li>
<li>Meaning: "Children are bound to cause their parents anxiety, and may or may not also bring them joy."</li>
<li>Source for meaning of English equivalent: <cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMartin_H._Manser2007">Martin H. Manser&#32;(2007).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=fgaUQc8NbTYC&amp;pg=PA40">The Facts on File Dictionary of Proverbs</a></i>. Infobase Publishing. p.&#160;40. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780816066735" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 978-0-8160-6673-5</a><span class="reference-accessdate">.&#32;Retrieved on 2 August 2013</span>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Facts+on+File+Dictionary+of+Proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Martin+H.+Manser&amp;rft.au=Martin+H.+Manser&amp;rft.date=2007&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B40&amp;rft.pub=Infobase+Publishing&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-8160-6673-5&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DfgaUQc8NbTYC%26pg%3DPA40&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;654. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B654&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Intemperans adulescentia effetum corpus tradit senectuti.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: They who would be young when they are old must be old when they are young.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;"1605".&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>. <b>II</b>. Routledge. p.&#160;1151. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.btitle=1605&amp;rft.atitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.volume=II&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B1151&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Inter gladium et iugulum.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Don't go between the tree and the bark.</li>
<li>Meaning: Do not interfere when two parts are having an argument.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;729. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B729&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Interdum stultus bene loquitur.'</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: ”A fool may give a wise man counsel.”</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1998">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1998).&#32;<i>Concise Dictionary of European Proverbs</i>&#32;(Abbreviated ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;40. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415160502" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415160502</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Concise+Dictionary+of+European+Proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1998&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B40&amp;rft.edition=Abbreviated&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415160502&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Ira furor brevis est.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "Anger is brief insanity" (<a href="/wiki/Horace" title="Horace">Horace</a>, epistles I, 2, 62).</li>
<li>Meaning: If you are mad, count to twenty.</li>
<li>Stone, J. R. (2005). The Routledge Dictionary of Latin Quotations: The Illiterati's Guide to Latin Maxims, Mottoes, Proverbs and Sayings, Routledge.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Iter per praecepta longum, per exempla, breve et efficax.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Example is better than precept.</li>
<li>"Every man I meet is in some way my superior; and in that I can learn of him."</li>
<li>Ralph Waldo Emerson, As quoted in <i>Think</i>, Vol. 4-5 (1938), p. 32</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMawr1885">Mawr, E.B.&#32;(1885).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://editura.mttlc.ro/carti/mawr-analogous-proverbs.pdf">Analogous Proverbs in Ten Languages</a></i>. p.&#160;28.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Analogous+Proverbs+in+Ten+Languages&amp;rft.aulast=Mawr&amp;rft.aufirst=E.B.&amp;rft.au=Mawr%2C+E.B.&amp;rft.date=1885&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B28&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Feditura.mttlc.ro%2Fcarti%2Fmawr-analogous-proverbs.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Iucundum est narrare sua mala.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: A problem shared is a problem halved.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;351. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B351&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="K">K</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latin_proverbs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: K">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The letter "k" was not commonly used in Classical Latin.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="L">L</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latin_proverbs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: L">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li>"Latet enim veritas, sed nihil pretiosius veritate" Francisco Sanchez de las Brozas (Minerva I, 1, 40, 16).
<ul><li>Translation: "Truth is hidden, but nothing is more beautiful than the truth”</li>
<li>"As to the quantity of absolute <a href="/wiki/Truth" title="Truth">truth</a> in a <a href="/wiki/Thought" title="Thought">thought</a>: it seems to me the more comprehensive and unobjectionable a thought becomes, the more clumsy and unexciting it gets. I like half-truths of a certain kind — they are interesting and they stimulate."</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Eric_Hoffer" title="Eric Hoffer">Eric Hoffer</a>, <i>Entry</i> (1950)</li>
<li>de las Brozas, F. S. (1754). Minerva, sive de causis latinae linguae commentarius.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Lumen soli mutuum das.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: You are lending light to the sun.</li>
<li>Note: Said of persons who affect to explain what is perfectly clear and intelligible.</li>
<li>Source of proverb &amp; meaning: H. T. Riley <i>Dictionary of Latin Quotations, Proverbs, Maxims, and Mottos, &amp;c.</i> (1866), p. 210.</li></ul></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="M">M</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latin_proverbs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: M">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><br />
</p>
<ul><li><i>Macte animo! Generose puer sic itur ad astra!</i>
<ul><li><i>Translation: "Be strong, young man! Through this way one gets to the stars." (Motto of the Brazilian Air Force Academy)</i></li>
<li>Chateaubriand, F. R. and A. T. de Mattos (1902). The memoirs of François René, vicomte de Chateaubriand, sometime ambassador to England: being a translation by Alexander Teixeira de Mattos of the Mémoires d'outre-tombe, with illustrations from contemporary sources, Freemantle and co.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Mala herba cito crescit</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "Weeds grow fast.”</li>
<li>Bezemer, K. (2005). Pierre de Belleperche: Portrait of a Legal Puritan, Klostermann.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Mala hostibus eveniant.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Shame take him that shame thinketh.</li>
<li>"Never attribute to malice that which is adequately explained by stupidity."</li>
<li>Robert J. Hanlon, <i>Murphy's Law Book Two&#160;: More Reasons Why Things Go Wrong!</i> (1980)</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;entry 806. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3Bentry+806&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Mali principii malus finis.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: Bad beginnings lead to bad results.</li>
<li>English equivalent: A bad beginning makes a bad ending.</li>
<li>"It is as impossible that a system radically erroneous, once commenced, should end well, as it is that a mathematical problem, commenced wrong, should come out right."</li>
<li>Source for meaning: <cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFWilliam_Henry_Porter1845">William Henry Porter&#32;(1845).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=KA4oAAAAYAAJ&amp;pg=PA202">Proverbs: Arranged in Alphabetical Order ...</a></i>. Munroe and Company. p.&#160;202.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Proverbs%3A+Arranged+in+Alphabetical+Order+...&amp;rft.aulast=William+Henry+Porter&amp;rft.au=William+Henry+Porter&amp;rft.date=1845&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B202&amp;rft.pub=Munroe+and+Company&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DKA4oAAAAYAAJ%26pg%3DPA202&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book"><i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=sso3AAAAYAAJ&amp;pg=PA214">Latin proverbs and quotations: With translations and parallel passages and a copious English index</a></i>. S. Low, son, and Marston. 1869. p.&#160;214.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Latin+proverbs+and+quotations%3A+With+translations+and+parallel+passages+and+a+copious+English+index&amp;rft.date=1869&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B214&amp;rft.pub=S.+Low%2C+son%2C+and+Marston&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3Dsso3AAAAYAAJ%26pg%3DPA214&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Malum consilium quod mutari non potest.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "It is a bad plan that cannot be changed (A plan that cannot be changed is a bad one).”</li>
<li>Stone, J. R. (2005). The Routledge Dictionary of Latin Quotations: The Illiterati's Guide to Latin Maxims, Mottoes, Proverbs and Sayings, Routledge</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Malo nodo malus quaerendus cuneus.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Desperate diseases must have desperate remedies.</li>
<li>Meaning: "Drastic action is called for – and justified – when you find yourself in a particularly difficult situation."</li>
<li>Source for meaning of English equivalent: <cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMartin_H._Manser2007">Martin H. Manser&#32;(2007).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=fgaUQc8NbTYC&amp;pg=PA53">The Facts on File Dictionary of Proverbs</a></i>. Infobase Publishing. p.&#160;53. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780816066735" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 978-0-8160-6673-5</a><span class="reference-accessdate">.&#32;Retrieved on 10 August 2013</span>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Facts+on+File+Dictionary+of+Proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Martin+H.+Manser&amp;rft.au=Martin+H.+Manser&amp;rft.date=2007&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B53&amp;rft.pub=Infobase+Publishing&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-8160-6673-5&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DfgaUQc8NbTYC%26pg%3DPA53&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFEmanuel_Strauss1994">Emanuel Strauss&#32;(1994).&#32;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=sm96Wlt8Ql0C&amp;pg=PT552">"812"</a>.&#32;<i>Concise Dictionary of European Proverbs</i>. Routledge. p.&#160;552. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9781136789786" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 978-1-136-78978-6</a><span class="reference-accessdate">.&#32;Retrieved on 10 August 2013</span>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.btitle=812&amp;rft.atitle=Concise+Dictionary+of+European+Proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Emanuel+Strauss&amp;rft.au=Emanuel+Strauss&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B552&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-136-78978-6&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3Dsm96Wlt8Ql0C%26pg%3DPT552&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Malum quidem nullum esse sine aliquo bono.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "There is, to be sure, no evil without something good.”</li>
<li>Watasin, E. The Dark Victorian: Risen, A-Girl Studio.</li>
<li>English equivalent: Every cloud has its silver lining.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Manus manum lavat</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "One hand washes the other.”</li>
<li>Houdt, T. (2002). Self-Presentation and Social Identification: The Rhetoric and Pragmatics of Letter Writing in Early Modern TImes, Leuven University Press.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Mater artium necessitas.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "Necessity is the mother of invention" (<a href="/wiki/Apuleius" title="Apuleius">Apuleius</a>)</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emmanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European Proverbs, Volym 1</i>. Routledge. p.&#160;989. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+Proverbs%2C+Volym+1&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emmanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emmanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B989&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Maxima debetur puero reverentia</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "One owes the greatest possible care for the child" (<a href="/wiki/Juvenal" title="Juvenal">Juvenal</a>)</li>
<li>Tegnér, E. and L. F. C. W. Böttiger (1849). Esaias Tegnérs samlade skrifter.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Medicus curat, natura sanat</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "The doctor cares [for his patient], nature heals [him]." or "Doctor cures, nature saves”</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emmanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European Proverbs, Volym 1</i>. Routledge. p.&#160;869. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+Proverbs%2C+Volym+1&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emmanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emmanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B869&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Melium est nomen bonum quam divitae multae.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: A good name is the best of all treasures.</li>
<li>"If a man has good corn, or wood, or boards, or pigs to sell, or can make better chairs or knives, crucibles, or church organs, than anybody else, you will find a broad, hard-beaten road to his house, tho it be in the woods. 'tis certain that the secret can not be kept: the first witness tells it to a second, and men go by fives and tens and fifties to his door."</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ralph_Waldo_Emerson" title="Ralph Waldo Emerson">Ralph Waldo Emerson</a>, <i>Works</i>, Volume VIII. In his Journal. (1855), p. 528. (Ed. 1912)</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1998">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1998).&#32;<i>Concise Dictionary of European Proverbs</i>&#32;(Abbreviated ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;33. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415160502" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415160502</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Concise+Dictionary+of+European+Proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1998&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B33&amp;rft.edition=Abbreviated&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415160502&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Memento mori.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: Remember that you are going to die.</li>
<li>"Death is a friend of ours; and he that is not ready to entertain him is not at home."</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Francis_Bacon" title="Francis Bacon">Francis Bacon</a>, <i>An Essay on Death</i> published in <i>The Remaines of the Right Honourable Francis Lord Verulam</i> (1648) but may not have been written by Bacon</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;1151. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B1151&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Mendacem memorem esse oportet.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: A liar should have a good memory.</li>
<li>Meaning: "Liars must remember the untruths they have told, to avoid contradicting themselves at some later date."</li>
<li>Source for meaning of English equivalent: <cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMartin_H._Manser2007">Martin H. Manser&#32;(2007).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=fgaUQc8NbTYC&amp;pg=PA167">The Facts on File Dictionary of Proverbs</a></i>. Infobase Publishing. p.&#160;167. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780816066735" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 978-0-8160-6673-5</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Facts+on+File+Dictionary+of+Proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Martin+H.+Manser&amp;rft.au=Martin+H.+Manser&amp;rft.date=2007&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B167&amp;rft.pub=Infobase+Publishing&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-8160-6673-5&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DfgaUQc8NbTYC%26pg%3DPA167&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=86yPOGG3YfcC&amp;pg=PT736">"274"</a>.&#32;<i>Dictionary of European Proverbs</i>. <b>I</b>. Routledge. p.&#160;257. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9781134864607" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 978-1-134-86460-7</a><span class="reference-accessdate">.&#32;Retrieved on 24 November 2013</span>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.btitle=274&amp;rft.atitle=Dictionary+of+European+Proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.volume=I&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B257&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-134-86460-7&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3D86yPOGG3YfcC%26pg%3DPT736&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Mens regnum bona possidet.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: His own desire leads every man.</li>
<li>"There is nothing man will not attempt when great enterprises hold out the promise of great rewards."</li>
<li>Livy, <i>History of Rome</i></li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;977. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B977&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Merx ultronea putet.</i>
<ul><li>Translation and English equivalent: Proffered service stinks.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book"><i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=5EEAAAAAYAAJ&amp;pg=PA201">Proverbs, Chiefly Taken from the Adagia of Erasmus with Explanations: And Further Illustrated by Corresponding Examples from the Spanish, Italian, French &amp; English Languages</a></i>. T. Egerton. 1814. p.&#160;201.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Proverbs%2C+Chiefly+Taken+from+the+Adagia+of+Erasmus+with+Explanations%3A+And+Further+Illustrated+by+Corresponding+Examples+from+the+Spanish%2C+Italian%2C+French+%26+English+Languages&amp;rft.date=1814&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B201&amp;rft.pub=T.+Egerton&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3D5EEAAAAAYAAJ%26pg%3DPA201&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Misera fortuna, qui caret inimico.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: It is a wretched fate which is absent <b><a href="/wiki/Enemies" title="Enemies">enemies</a></b>.</li>
<li>English equivalent: If you have no <b><a href="/wiki/Enemies" title="Enemies">enemies</a></b> it is a sign that fortune has forgotten you; People throw stones only at trees with fruit on them.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;1008. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B1008&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Mobiles ad superstitionem perculsae semel mentes</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "Minds once cowed are prone to superstition."</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tacitus" title="Tacitus">Tacitus</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Agricola_(book)" class="extiw" title="w:Agricola (book)">"Agricola"</a>, 1.28</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Mulier est hominis confusio.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "Woman is man's ruin."</li>
<li>"Part of a comic definition of woman" from the Altercatio Hadriani Augusti et Secundi.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Famously quoted by Chauntecleer in <a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_Chaucer" title="Geoffrey Chaucer">Geoffrey Chaucer</a>'s <i>Canterbury Tales’’.</i></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Multum clamoris, parum lanae.</i>
<ul><li>Translation and English equivalent: Great cry and little wool.</li>
<li>Meaning: "Much ado about nothing."</li>
<li>Source for meaning of English equivalent: <cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFKeating1859">Keating, Walter&#32;(1859).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=PdxtAAAAMAAJ&amp;pg=PA128">Proverbs of All Nations</a></i>. W. Kent &amp; Company (late D. Bogue). p.&#160;128.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Proverbs+of+All+Nations&amp;rft.aulast=Keating&amp;rft.aufirst=Walter&amp;rft.au=Keating%2C+Walter&amp;rft.date=1859&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B128&amp;rft.pub=W.+Kent+%26+Company+%28late+D.+Bogue%29&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DPdxtAAAAMAAJ%26pg%3DPA128&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=86yPOGG3YfcC&amp;pg=PT499">"178"</a>.&#32;<i>Dictionary of European Proverbs</i>. <b>II</b>. Routledge. p.&#160;173. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9781134864607" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 978-1-134-86460-7</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.btitle=178&amp;rft.atitle=Dictionary+of+European+Proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.volume=II&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B173&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-134-86460-7&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3D86yPOGG3YfcC%26pg%3DPT499&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Mundus vult decipi, ergo decipiatur.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: The world desires to be deceived; therefore it is. (Attributed to <a href="/wiki/Petronius_Arbiter" class="mw-redirect" title="Petronius Arbiter">Petronius</a>)</li>
<li>English equivalent: The world wants to be taken in.</li>
<li>Thompson, J., C. The University of Arizona. Rhetoric, et al. (2008). "A Kind of Thing that Might Be": Toward a Poetics of New Media, University of Arizona.</li></ul></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="N">N</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latin_proverbs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: N">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><i>Ne eligat is qui donum accipit.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Beggars can’t be choosers.</li>
<li>"We must accept with gratitude and without complaint what we are given when we do not have the means or opportunity to provide ourselves with something better.”</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMartin_H._Manser2007">Martin H. Manser&#32;(2007).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=fgaUQc8NbTYC&amp;pg=PA19">The Facts on File Dictionary of Proverbs</a></i>. Infobase Publishing. p.&#160;19. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780816066735" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 978-0-8160-6673-5</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Facts+on+File+Dictionary+of+Proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Martin+H.+Manser&amp;rft.au=Martin+H.+Manser&amp;rft.date=2007&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B19&amp;rft.pub=Infobase+Publishing&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-8160-6673-5&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DfgaUQc8NbTYC%26pg%3DPA19&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMawr1885">Mawr, E.B.&#32;(1885).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://editura.mttlc.ro/carti/mawr-analogous-proverbs.pdf">Analogous Proverbs in Ten Languages</a></i>. p.&#160;16.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Analogous+Proverbs+in+Ten+Languages&amp;rft.aulast=Mawr&amp;rft.aufirst=E.B.&amp;rft.au=Mawr%2C+E.B.&amp;rft.date=1885&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B16&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Feditura.mttlc.ro%2Fcarti%2Fmawr-analogous-proverbs.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Ne puero gladium.</i>
<ul><li>Do not give a child a sword.</li>
<li>H. T. Riley <i>Dictionary of Latin Quotations, Proverbs, Maxims, and Mottos, &amp;c.</i> (1866), p. 249.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Ne quid expectes amicos, quod tute agere possis.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: Expect nothing from friends, do what you can do yourself.</li>
<li>English equivalent: For what thou canst do thyself, rely not on another.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;600. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B600&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Ne quid nimis</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "Nothing too much", moderation in all thing (<a href="/wiki/Terence" title="Terence">Terence</a>)</li>
<li>"Work and play they're never okay to mix."</li>
<li>Jimmy Eat World taken from their song "Work".</li>
<li>Kierkegaard, S. (2008). Sickness Unto Death, Wilder Publications.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Ne sutor supra crepidam</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: A blind man should not judge of colours.</li>
<li>"An uneducated man cannot judge of the attainments of the learned."</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFM._W._Carr1868">M. W. Carr&#32;(1868).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=oJw-AAAAcAAJ&amp;pg=PA141">A Collection of Telugu Proverbs translated, illustrated and explained; together with some Sanscrit Proverbs printed in the Devanâgarî and Telugu Characters: By M.
