Christian Knowledge Society's Press. p.&#160;141.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=A+Collection+of+Telugu+Proverbs+translated%2C+illustrated+and+explained%3B+together+with+some+Sanscrit+Proverbs+printed+in+the+Devan%C3%A2gar%C3%AE+and+Telugu+Characters%3A+By+M.+W.+Carr.+A+Supplement+to+the+Collection+of+Telugu+Proverbs%3A+containing+additional+Proverbs%2C+an+Index+verborum%2C+and+an+index+to+the+European+Proverbs+quoted+in+illustration&amp;rft.aulast=M.+W.+Carr&amp;rft.au=M.+W.+Carr&amp;rft.date=1868&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B141&amp;rft.pub=Christian+Knowledge+Society%27s+Press&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DoJw-AAAAcAAJ%26pg%3DPA141&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li>
<li>Carlyle, T., J. Ruskin, et al. (1982). The Correspondence of Thomas Carlyle and John Ruskin, Stanford University Press.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Nemo regere potest nisi qui et regi.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Who has not served cannot command.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;758. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B758&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Nemo iudex in causa sua.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "No one is a judge in his own case".</li>
<li>Boczek, B. A. (2005). International Law: A Dictionary, Scarecrow Press.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Nescis quid serus vesper vehat.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "You know not what night-fall may bring."</li>
<li>H. T. Riley <i>Dictionary of Latin Quotations, Proverbs, Maxims, and Mottos, &amp;c.</i> (1866), p. 261.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Nihil ægrius quam disciplinam accipimus.</i>
<ul><li>Translation:  We receive nothing with so much reluctance as instruction.</li>
<li>Note: Specified as a Roman proverb in the source.</li>
<li>English equivalent: Advice most needed is the least heeded.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStone2006">Stone&#32;(2006).&#32;<i>Routledge Dictionary of World Proverbs</i>. Taylor \&amp; Francis. p.&#160;8.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Routledge+Dictionary+of+World+Proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Stone&amp;rft.au=Stone&amp;rft.date=2006&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B8&amp;rft.pub=Taylor+%5C%26+Francis&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Nitidae vestes ornatiorem reddunt.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Fine feathers make fine birds.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMawr1885">Mawr, E.B.&#32;(1885).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://editura.mttlc.ro/carti/mawr-analogous-proverbs.pdf">Analogous Proverbs in Ten Languages</a></i>. p.&#160;30.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Analogous+Proverbs+in+Ten+Languages&amp;rft.aulast=Mawr&amp;rft.aufirst=E.B.&amp;rft.au=Mawr%2C+E.B.&amp;rft.date=1885&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B30&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Feditura.mttlc.ro%2Fcarti%2Fmawr-analogous-proverbs.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>In nocte consilium.</i>
<ul><li>The night brings counsel.</li>
<li>English equivalent: Take counsel of one's pillow.</li>
<li>Note: Specified as a Latin proverb in the source.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFKelly1859">Kelly, Walter Keating&#32;(1859).&#32;<i>Proverbs of all nations</i>&#32;(W. Kent &amp; co. (late D. Bogue) ed.). p.&#160;63.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Proverbs+of+all+nations&amp;rft.aulast=Kelly&amp;rft.aufirst=Walter+Keating&amp;rft.au=Kelly%2C+Walter+Keating&amp;rft.date=1859&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B63&amp;rft.edition=W.+Kent+%26+co.+%28late+D.+Bogue%29&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Non alios suo modulo metiri.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Do not judge others by your own yardstick.</li>
<li>:Those who understand evil pardon it."</li>
<li>George Bernard Shaw, <i>Maxims for Revolutionists</i> (1903)</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMawr1885">Mawr, E.B.&#32;(1885).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://editura.mttlc.ro/carti/mawr-analogous-proverbs.pdf">Analogous Proverbs in Ten Languages</a></i>. p.&#160;22.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Analogous+Proverbs+in+Ten+Languages&amp;rft.aulast=Mawr&amp;rft.aufirst=E.B.&amp;rft.au=Mawr%2C+E.B.&amp;rft.date=1885&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B22&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Feditura.mttlc.ro%2Fcarti%2Fmawr-analogous-proverbs.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Non capiunt lepores tympana rauca leves.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Drumming is not the way to catch a hare.</li>
<li>Meaning: Don't expect anyone to change his ways by scolding him.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;754. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B754&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Nocere facile est, prodesse difficile.</i>
<ul><li>English translation: It is easy to do harm, difficult to do good. <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://books.google.ca/books?id=ujfWAAAAMAAJ&amp;pg=PA117&amp;lpg=PA117&amp;dq=nocere+facile+prodesse+difficile&amp;source=bl&amp;ots=nvAjqax7nl&amp;sig=lD4ORf80MDQl-QUmerbKBpRJUmQ&amp;hl=en&amp;sa=X&amp;ved=2ahUKEwjjsMGXwYDbAhVlmuAKHV9GChEQ6AEwB3oECAEQAQ#v=onepage&amp;q=nocere%20facile%20prodesse%20difficile&amp;f=false">[2]</a></li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;718. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B718&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Non nobis solum nati sumus</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "We are not born for ourselves alone”</li>
<li>Meaning: Each one of us carries a responsibility for the whole world.</li>
<li>Stone, J. R. (2005). The Routledge Dictionary of Latin Quotations: The Illiterati's Guide to Latin Maxims, Mottoes, Proverbs and Sayings, Routledge.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Non olet</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "It [money] doesn't smell" (according to <a href="/wiki/Suetonius" title="Suetonius">Suetonius</a>, Emperor <a href="/wiki/Vespasian" title="Vespasian">Vespasian</a> was challenged by his son Titus for taxing the public lavatories,  the emperor held up a coin before his son and asked whether it smelled)</li>
<li>Ferlosio, R. S. (2005). Non olet, Destino.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Non opus est follo suspendere tympana collo.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: A fool does not need any bells.</li>
<li>English equivalent: A tongue of a fool carves a piece of his heart to all that sit near him.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;136. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B136&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Non quia difficilia sunt non audemus, sed quia non audemus, difficilia sunt.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "It is not because things are difficult that we do not dare, but because we do not dare, things are difficult." (<a href="/wiki/Seneca_the_Younger" title="Seneca the Younger">Seneca</a>, Letter to Lucilius, letter 104, section 26, line 5)</li>
<li>Gresley, W. (1835). Ecclesiastes Anglicanus: being a treatise on preaching, as adapted to a Church of England congregation&#160;: in a series of letters to a young clergyman, printed for J. G. F. &amp; J. Rivington.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Non scholae, sed vitae discimus.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "We learn not for school but for life." (<a href="/wiki/Seneca_the_Younger" title="Seneca the Younger">Seneca</a>'s original quotation is "Non vitae, sed scholae discimus.”)</li>
<li>"Education, therefore, is a process of living and not a preparation for future living."</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/John_Dewey" title="John Dewey">John Dewey</a>, <i><a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/My_Pedagogic_Creed#ARTICLE_TWO._WHAT_THE_SCHOOL_IS" class="extiw" title="wikisource:My Pedagogic Creed">My Pedagogic Creed</a></i> (1897)</li>
<li>Stone, J. R. (2005). The Routledge Dictionary of Latin Quotations: The Illiterati's Guide to Latin Maxims, Mottoes, Proverbs and Sayings, Routledge.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Non semper erit aestas.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "It will not always be summer." (be prepared for hard times)</li>
<li>Stone, J. R. (2005). The Routledge Dictionary of Latin Quotations: The Illiterati's Guide to Latin Maxims, Mottoes, Proverbs and Sayings, Routledge.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Nulla poena sine lege</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "No punishment without a law.”</li>
<li>Nulla Poena Sine Lege. E.j. Brill, Leiden 1934, Brill Archive.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Nulla regula sine exceptione.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "No rule without exception.”</li>
<li>(1869). Hygiea.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Nulli tacuisse nocet, tutum silentii premium.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Least said, soonest mended.</li>
<li>Meaning: "In private animosities and verbal contentions, where angry passions are apt to rise, and irritating, if not profane expressions are often made use of, as we sometimes see to be the case, not only among neighbors, but in families, between husbands and wives, or parents and children, or the children themselves and other members of the household, - the least said, the better in general. By multiplying words, cases often grow worse instead of better."</li>
<li>Source for meaning of English equivalent: <cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFPorter1845">Porter, William Henry&#32;(1845).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=KA4oAAAAYAAJ&amp;pg=PA125">Proverbs: Arranged in Alphabetical Order ...</a></i>. Munroe and Company. pp.&#160;125.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Proverbs%3A+Arranged+in+Alphabetical+Order+...&amp;rft.aulast=Porter&amp;rft.aufirst=William+Henry&amp;rft.au=Porter%2C+William+Henry&amp;rft.date=1845&amp;rft.pages=pp.%26nbsp%3B125&amp;rft.pub=Munroe+and+Company&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DKA4oAAAAYAAJ%26pg%3DPA125&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMawr1885">Mawr, E.B.&#32;(1885).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://editura.mttlc.ro/carti/mawr-analogous-proverbs.pdf">Analogous Proverbs in Ten Languages</a></i>. p.&#160;53.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Analogous+Proverbs+in+Ten+Languages&amp;rft.aulast=Mawr&amp;rft.aufirst=E.B.&amp;rft.au=Mawr%2C+E.B.&amp;rft.date=1885&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B53&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Feditura.mttlc.ro%2Fcarti%2Fmawr-analogous-proverbs.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Nullus est liber tam mallus, ut non aliqua parte prosit.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: No book was so bad, but some good might be got out of it.</li>
<li>Meaning: You might typically get something good out of an overall faulty book, especially a non fictional one, such as sound advice or anecdotes to tell others.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;1104. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B1104&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="O">O</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latin_proverbs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: O">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><i>Oblata arripe.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: When the pig is proffered, hold up the poke.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;1226. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B1226&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Occidit miseros crambe repetita magistros.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Take heed of enemies reconciled and of meat twice boiled.</li>
<li>Meaning: Your former enemies might cunningly take revenge on you just out of spite.; Trust not a reconciled enemy more than an open foe.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1998">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1998).&#32;<i>Concise Dictionary of European Proverbs</i>&#32;(Abbreviated ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;25. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415160502" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415160502</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Concise+Dictionary+of+European+Proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1998&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B25&amp;rft.edition=Abbreviated&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415160502&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Oculus animi index.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: Eyes are the index of the mind.</li>
<li>English equivalent: The eye looks but it is the mind that sees.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;1175. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B1175&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Omnia cum pretio.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: All things (in rome) have their price. Original "omnia Romae cum pretio" Juvenal</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;1111. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B1111&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Omnibus se accomodat rebus, omnia novit.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: He who applies himself to all things, knows all things.</li>
<li>English equivalent: All is fish that comes to net.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMawr1885">Mawr, E.B.&#32;(1885).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://editura.mttlc.ro/carti/mawr-analogous-proverbs.pdf">Analogous Proverbs in Ten Languages</a></i>. p.&#160;4.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Analogous+Proverbs+in+Ten+Languages&amp;rft.aulast=Mawr&amp;rft.aufirst=E.B.&amp;rft.au=Mawr%2C+E.B.&amp;rft.date=1885&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B4&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Feditura.mttlc.ro%2Fcarti%2Fmawr-analogous-proverbs.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Omnium artium medicina nobilissima est.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: Medicine is the noblest of all arts.</li>
<li>Lautenbach, E. (2002). Latein-Deutsch: Zitaten-Lexikon: Quellennachweise, Lit.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Onorate il senno antico.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Grey hairs are honorable.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMawr1885">Mawr, E.B.&#32;(1885).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://editura.mttlc.ro/carti/mawr-analogous-proverbs.pdf">Analogous Proverbs in Ten Languages</a></i>. p.&#160;35.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Analogous+Proverbs+in+Ten+Languages&amp;rft.aulast=Mawr&amp;rft.aufirst=E.B.&amp;rft.au=Mawr%2C+E.B.&amp;rft.date=1885&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B35&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Feditura.mttlc.ro%2Fcarti%2Fmawr-analogous-proverbs.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Oratores fuint, poetae nascuntur.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Poets are born, but orators are trained.</li>
<li>Meaning: Some things can be improved by training, others require innate talent.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1998">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1998).&#32;<i>Concise Dictionary of European Proverbs</i>&#32;(Abbreviated ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;331. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415160502" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415160502</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Concise+Dictionary+of+European+Proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1998&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B331&amp;rft.edition=Abbreviated&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415160502&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Optimi natatores saepius submerguntur.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Good swimmers are often drowned.</li>
<li>Meaning: Beware of letting your competence lead you into overconfidence.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;879. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B879&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Optimum medicamentum quies est.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: Rest is the best medicine.</li>
<li>Arnott, J. (1845). Appendix to an essay on therapeutical inquiry, containing the application of plans of treatment noticed therein to the practice of midwifery.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Otia dant vitia.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Idle hands are the devils playthings.</li>
<li>"No thoroughly occupied man was ever yet very miserable."</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Letitia_Elizabeth_Landon" title="Letitia Elizabeth Landon">Letitia Elizabeth Landon</a> <i>Romance and Reality</i> (1831) Vol. II, page 108</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;710. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B710&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="P">P</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latin_proverbs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: P">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><i>Pacta sunt servanda</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "Agreements must be honoured.”</li>
<li>Hasan, A. M. (2005). Pacta sunt servanda: the principle and its application in petroleum production sharing contract, Fikahati Aneska.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Pars est beneficii quod petitur si cito neges.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: A prompt refusal has in part the grace of a favour granted.</li>
<li>"Friendship ... flourishes not so much by kindnesses as by sincerity."</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/%C3%89tienne_de_la_Bo%C3%A9tie" class="mw-redirect" title="Étienne de la Boétie">Étienne de la Boétie</a>, <i>Discourse of Voluntary Servitude</i>, Part 3</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFKelly1859">Kelly, Walter Keating&#32;(1859).&#32;<i>Proverbs of all nations</i>&#32;(W. Kent &amp; co. (late D. Bogue) ed.). p.&#160;147.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Proverbs+of+all+nations&amp;rft.aulast=Kelly&amp;rft.aufirst=Walter+Keating&amp;rft.au=Kelly%2C+Walter+Keating&amp;rft.date=1859&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B147&amp;rft.edition=W.+Kent+%26+co.+%28late+D.+Bogue%29&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Pax melior est quam iustissimum bellum.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "Peace is better than the most just war.”</li>
<li>Clure, A. M. Les HazArts Légendaires, Annie Mc Clure.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Pede poena claudo.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "Punishment comes limping."</li>
<li>English equivalent: Punishment is lame, but it comes.</li>
<li>Valerius, J. D. (1855). Samlade vitterhets-arbeten, Norstedt.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Periculum in mora.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: [There's] danger in delay. (<a href="/wiki/Livy" title="Livy">Livy</a>)</li>
<li>English equivalent: Delays are dangerous.</li>
<li>Meaning: "Hesitation or procastination may lead to trouble or disaster."</li>
<li>Source for meaning of English equivalent: <cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMartin_H._Manser2007">Martin H. Manser&#32;(2007).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=fgaUQc8NbTYC&amp;pg=PA53">The Facts on File Dictionary of Proverbs</a></i>. Infobase Publishing. p.&#160;53. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780816066735" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 978-0-8160-6673-5</a><span class="reference-accessdate">.&#32;Retrieved on 10 August 2013</span>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Facts+on+File+Dictionary+of+Proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Martin+H.+Manser&amp;rft.au=Martin+H.+Manser&amp;rft.date=2007&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B53&amp;rft.pub=Infobase+Publishing&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-8160-6673-5&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DfgaUQc8NbTYC%26pg%3DPA53&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li>
<li>Ruder, G. (1766). Om rikets swåra öde, och huru det kan förekommas. Periculum in mora.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Philosophum non facit barba.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "A beard doesn't make a philosopher." (<a href="/wiki/Plutarch" title="Plutarch">Plutarch</a>)</li>
<li>'"The educated don't get that way by memorizing <a href="/wiki/Facts" class="mw-redirect" title="Facts">facts</a>; they get that way by respecting them."</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tom_Heehler" title="Tom Heehler">Tom Heehler</a>, <i>The Well-Spoken Thesaurus</i> (2011).</li>
<li>Source: <cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1998">Strauss, Emmanuel&#32;(1998).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European Proverbs</i>. Routledge. p.&#160;117. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415160502" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415160502</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+Proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emmanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emmanuel&amp;rft.date=1998&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B117&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415160502&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Plus ultra</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "Further Beyond”, Spanish Motto.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Piscem vorat maior minorem.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: The large fishes eats the small ones.</li>
<li>Meaning: "Small organizations or insignificant people tend to be swallowed up or destroyed by those that are greater and more powerful."</li>
<li>Source for meaning: <cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMartin_H._Manser2007">Martin H. Manser&#32;(2007).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=fgaUQc8NbTYC&amp;pg=PA358">The Facts on File Dictionary of Proverbs</a></i>. Infobase Publishing. p.&#160;27. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780816066735" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 978-0-8160-6673-5</a><span class="reference-accessdate">.&#32;Retrieved on 1 July 2013</span>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Facts+on+File+Dictionary+of+Proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Martin+H.+Manser&amp;rft.au=Martin+H.+Manser&amp;rft.date=2007&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B27&amp;rft.pub=Infobase+Publishing&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-8160-6673-5&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DfgaUQc8NbTYC%26pg%3DPA358&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;1086. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B1086&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Post prandium stabis, post coenam ambulabis.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "After dinner, rest a while, after supper walk a mile."</li>
<li>Source: <cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFHugh_Moore1831">Hugh Moore&#32;(1831).&#32;<i>A Dictionary of Quotations</i>. p.&#160;314.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=A+Dictionary+of+Quotations&amp;rft.aulast=Hugh+Moore&amp;rft.au=Hugh+Moore&amp;rft.date=1831&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B314&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Potius sero quam numquam</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "Better late then never" (<a href="/wiki/Livy" title="Livy">Livy</a>)</li>
<li>Source: <cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1998">Strauss, Emmanuel&#32;(1998).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European Proverbs</i>. Routledge. p.&#160;166. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415160502" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415160502</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+Proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emmanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emmanuel&amp;rft.date=1998&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B166&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415160502&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Praemonitus, praemunitus</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "Forewarned (is) forearmed”</li>
<li>Source: <cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1998">Strauss, Emmanuel&#32;(1998).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European Proverbs</i>. Routledge. p.&#160;563. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415160502" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415160502</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+Proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emmanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emmanuel&amp;rft.date=1998&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B563&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415160502&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Praesentem mulge, fugientem quid insequeris.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: Milk today, for what you are aiming for is fleeing.</li>
<li>English equivalent: One today is worth two tomorrows.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;1137. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B1137&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Praestat cautela quam medela.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Prevention is better than cure.</li>
<li>Meaning: Precaution is infinitely better than remedial measures.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;881. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B881&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Praemonitus, praemunitus.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Forewarned, forearmed.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=86yPOGG3YfcC&amp;pg=PT1042">"401"</a>.&#32;<i>Dictionary of European Proverbs</i>. <b>I</b>. Routledge. p.&#160;364. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9781134864607" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 978-1-134-86460-7</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.btitle=401&amp;rft.atitle=Dictionary+of+European+Proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.volume=I&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B364&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-134-86460-7&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3D86yPOGG3YfcC%26pg%3DPT1042&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Publica fama non semper vana.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: Provided common, commonly true.</li>
<li>English equivalent: Common fame is often to blame.</li>
<li>Meaning: A general disrepute is often true.</li>
<li>Source for meaning of English equivalent: <cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMartin_H._Manser2007">Martin H. Manser&#32;(2007).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=fgaUQc8NbTYC&amp;pg=PA45">The Facts on File Dictionary of Proverbs</a></i>. Infobase Publishing. p.&#160;45. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780816066735" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 978-0-8160-6673-5</a><span class="reference-accessdate">.&#32;Retrieved on 4 August 2013</span>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Facts+on+File+Dictionary+of+Proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Martin+H.+Manser&amp;rft.au=Martin+H.+Manser&amp;rft.date=2007&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B45&amp;rft.pub=Infobase+Publishing&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-8160-6673-5&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DfgaUQc8NbTYC%26pg%3DPA45&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;662. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B662&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Pulverulenta novis bene verritur area scopis.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: "New brooms sweep clean."</li>
<li>Meaning: Newcomers are the most ambitious.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;1103. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B1103&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Q">Q</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latin_proverbs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Q">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><i>Qualis rex, talis grex</i>
<ul><li>Translation: Like king, like people.</li>
<li>"The people are fashioned according to the example of their kings; and edicts are of less power than the life of the ruler."</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Claudianus" class="mw-redirect" title="Claudianus">Claudianus</a>, <i>De Quarto Consulatu Honorii Augustii Panegyris</i>, CCXCIX.</li>
<li>Stone, J. R. (2005). The Routledge Dictionary of Latin Quotations: The Illiterati's Guide to Latin Maxims, Mottoes, Proverbs and Sayings, Routledge.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Qualis pagatio, talis laboratio.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: What pay, such work.</li>
<li>English equivalent: You get what you pay for.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;494. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B494&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Quam bene vivas refert, non quam diu.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: How well you live makes a difference, not how long. (<a href="/wiki/Seneca" class="mw-disambig" title="Seneca">Seneca</a>)</li>
<li>Haase, W. and H. Temporini (1983). Aufstieg und Niedergang Der Römischen Welt: Geschichte und Kultur Roms Im Spiegel Der Neueren Forschung, Walter de Gruyter.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Quantum Satis.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: As much as needed, enough.</li>
<li>Rundkvist, A. (1968). Quantum satis: så mycket som är tillräckligt&#160;; aforismer, skaldeord och citat från skilda tider om livet och människan, Rundqvists Bokförlag.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Quem di diligunt, adulescens moritur</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "Whom the gods love dies young" (<a href="/wiki/Plautus" title="Plautus">Plautus</a>, Bacchides, IV, 7, 18). In the comic play, a sarcastic servant says this to his aging master. The rest of the sentence reads: <i>dum valet, sentit, sapit</i>, "while he is full of health, perception and judgement.”</li>
<li>Morris, G. (2009). Angel Train, B&amp;H Publishing Group.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Quem dii odere, paedagogum fecere</i> (also <i>Quem dii oderunt, paedagogum fecerunt</i>)
<ul><li>Translation: "Whom the gods hated, they made them pedagogues”</li>
<li>Moritz, K. P. Anton Reiser: Ein Psychologischer Roman, tredition.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Quis custodiet ipsos custodes?</i>
<ul><li>Translation:: Who watches the watchmen?</li>
<li><i>Satires</i> by Juvenal <a class="external autonumber" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Satires_(Juvenal)">[3]</a></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Qui dormit non peccat.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "He who sleeps does not sin”</li>
<li>Archer, P. and L. Archer 500 Foreign Words and Phrases You Should Know to Sound Smart: Terms to Demonstrate Your Savoir Faire, Chutzpah, and Bravado, F+W Media.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Qui habet aures audiendi audiat</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "Those who have ears to hear, hear!" (<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vulgate" class="extiw" title="w:Vulgate">Vulgate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gospel_of_Matthew" title="Gospel of Matthew">Matthew</a> 11:15)</li>
<li>English equivalent: Nature gave us two ears and one mouth.</li>
<li>Collins, J. F. (1985). A Primer of Ecclesiastical Latin, Catholic University of America Press.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Qui non est hodie, cras minus aptus erit.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: He who is not ready today, will be less so tomorrow.</li>
<li>English equivalent: He that will not when he may, when he will he may have nay.</li>
<li>Meaning: "Take advantage of an opportunity when it presents itself, even if you do not want or need it at the time, because it may no longer be available when you do."</li>
<li>Source for meaning of English equivalent:<cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMartin_H._Manser2007">Martin H. Manser&#32;(2007).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=fgaUQc8NbTYC&amp;pg=PA120">The Facts on File Dictionary of Proverbs</a></i>. Infobase Publishing. p.&#160;120. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780816066735" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 978-0-8160-6673-5</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Facts+on+File+Dictionary+of+Proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Martin+H.+Manser&amp;rft.au=Martin+H.+Manser&amp;rft.date=2007&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B120&amp;rft.pub=Infobase+Publishing&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-8160-6673-5&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DfgaUQc8NbTYC%26pg%3DPA120&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFKelly1859">Kelly, Walter Keating&#32;(1859).&#32;<i>Proverbs of all nations</i>. W. Kent &amp; co. (late D. Bogue). p.&#160;41.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Proverbs+of+all+nations&amp;rft.aulast=Kelly&amp;rft.aufirst=Walter+Keating&amp;rft.au=Kelly%2C+Walter+Keating&amp;rft.date=1859&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B41&amp;rft.pub=W.+Kent+%26+co.+%28late+D.+Bogue%29&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Qui me amat, amet et canem meum.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Love me, love my dog.</li>
<li>Meaning: If you love someone, you will virtually like everything about him.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;953. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B953&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Qui audet adipiscitur.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: He who dares wins.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFEkaterina_Walter2012">Ekaterina Walter&#32;(18 December 2012).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=J8Gjmoy2rbkC">Think Like Zuck: The Five Business Secrets of Facebook's Improbably Brilliant CEO Mark Zuckerberg</a></i>. McGraw Hill Professional. p.&#160;177. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780071809498" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 978-0-07-180949-8</a><span class="reference-accessdate">.&#32;Retrieved on 14 August 2013</span>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Think+Like+Zuck%3A+The+Five+Business+Secrets+of+Facebook%27s+Improbably+Brilliant+CEO+Mark+Zuckerberg&amp;rft.aulast=Ekaterina+Walter&amp;rft.au=Ekaterina+Walter&amp;rft.date=18+December+2012&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B177&amp;rft.pub=McGraw+Hill+Professional&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-07-180949-8&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DJ8Gjmoy2rbkC&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Qui multum habet, plus cupit.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: He who has much desires more. (<a href="/wiki/Seneca" class="mw-disambig" title="Seneca">Seneca</a>)</li>
<li>Swedish equivalent: Much wants more.</li>
<li>Jones, P. V. and K. C. Sidwell (1986). Reading Latin: Grammar, Vocabulary and Exercises, Cambridge University Press.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Qui nimis capit, parum stringit.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Don't have too many irons in the fire.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;977. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B977&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Qui non proficit, deficit.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "He who does not go forward, loses ground." or "He who does not accomplish anything, is a failure/has shortcomings.”</li>
<li>English equivalent: He who does not advance goes backwards.</li>
<li>Stone, J. R. (2005). The Routledge Dictionary of Latin Quotations: The Illiterati's Guide to Latin Maxims, Mottoes, Proverbs and Sayings, Routledge.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Qui primus venerit, primus verat.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: First come, first served.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMawr1885">Mawr, E.B.&#32;(1885).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://editura.mttlc.ro/carti/mawr-analogous-proverbs.pdf">Analogous Proverbs in Ten Languages</a></i>. p.&#160;32.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Analogous+Proverbs+in+Ten+Languages&amp;rft.aulast=Mawr&amp;rft.aufirst=E.B.&amp;rft.au=Mawr%2C+E.B.&amp;rft.date=1885&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B32&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Feditura.mttlc.ro%2Fcarti%2Fmawr-analogous-proverbs.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Qui pro innocente dicit, satis est eloquens.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "He who speaks for the innocent is eloquent enough." (<a href="/wiki/Publilius_Syrus" title="Publilius Syrus">Publilius Syrus</a>)</li>
<li>Chambers, P. L. (2007). Latin Alive and Well: An Introductory Text, University of Oklahoma Press.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Qui rogat, non errat.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "(One) who asks, doesn't err.”</li>
<li>English equivalent: <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/No_such_thing_as_a_stupid_question">The only stupid question is the one not asked.</a></li>
<li>Mimbar Altar, Kanisius.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Qui scribit, bis legit.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "Who <b><a href="/wiki/Write" class="mw-redirect" title="Write">writes</a></b>, reads twice.”</li>
<li>Stone, J. R. (2005). The Routledge Dictionary of Latin Quotations: The Illiterati's Guide to Latin Maxims, Mottoes, Proverbs and Sayings, Routledge.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Qui tacet consentire videtur, ubi loqui debuit ac potuit.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "Who is silent, when he ought to and might have spoken, is seen to agree.”</li>
<li>Schlesinger, R. B., P. G. Bonassies, et al. (1968). Formation of contracts: a study of the common core of legal systems, conducted under the auspices of the General principles of law project of the Cornell Law School, Oceana Publications.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Qui transtulit sustinet.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "He who transplanted still sustains." (motto of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Connecticut" class="extiw" title="w:Connecticut">Connecticut</a> referring to the transplantation of settlers from England to the New World.)</li>
<li>Caughman, G., J. Devine, et al. (1997). Qui Transtulit Sustinet.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Qui vitulum tollit, taurum subduxerit idem .</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: He that steals an egg will steal an ox.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;962. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B962&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Qui vult dare parva non debet magna rogare.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "He who wishes to give little shouldn't ask for much.”</li>
<li>Crawford, G. A. and U. o. M. L. Workshop (1963). Elementary Latin: the basic structures, University of Michigan Press.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Quidquid agis, prudenter agas, et respice finem!</i>
<ul><li>Translation: Whatever you do, may you do it prudently, and look to the end!</li>
<li>English equivalent: Whatever you do, act wisely, and consider the end.</li>
<li>Timmer, M. Van Anima tot Zeus / druk 1: encyclopedie van begrippen uit de mythologie, religie, alchemie, cultuurgeschiedenis en jungiaanse psychologie, Lemniscaat.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Quidquid discis, tibi discis</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "Whatever you learn, you learn it for yourself.”</li>
<li>Arbiter, P. and W. D. Lowe (1905). Petronii Cena Trimalchionis, D. Bell and co.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Quidquid latine dictum, altum videtur.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "Whatever is said in Latin seems profound."</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;965. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B965&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Quieta non movere</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "Don't move settled things" (i.e. "Don't rock the boat", "Let sleeping dogs lie.”)</li>
<li>McKenna, M. (1996). The Captive Republic: A History of Republicanism in Australia, 1788-1996, Cambridge University Press.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Quis custodiet ipsos custodes?</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "Who will watch the watchers themselves?" or "Who will guard the guardians themselves?" (<a href="/wiki/Juvenal" title="Juvenal">Juvenal</a>)</li>
<li>Brown-John, C. L. (1981). Canadian regulatory agencies: quis custodiet ipsos custodes?, Butterworths.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Quod gratis asseritur, gratis negatur.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: What is asserted gratuitously may be denied gratuitously.</li>
<li><i>Variants</i>:  What is asserted without evidence/proof/reason, may/can be dismissed/denied without evidence/proof/reason.</li>
<li>Jon R. Stone, <i>The Routledge Dictionary of Latin Quotations</i> (2005), p. 101. Anonymous, widely used since at least the early 19th century (e.g. <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Classical_Journal" class="extiw" title="w:The Classical Journal">The Classical Journal </a></i>, Vol. 40 (1829), <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=EhngAAAAMAAJ&amp;pg=PA312&amp;q=quod+gratis+asseritur+gratis+negatur,">p. 312</a>).</li>
<li>See also: <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hitchens%27s_razor" class="extiw" title="w:Hitchens&#39;s razor">Hitchens's razor</a></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Quod nocet, saepe docet</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "That which harms, often teaches”</li>
<li>Meaning: Unpleasant experiences will make you wiser.</li>
<li>English equivalent: What does not kill you makes you stronger.</li>
<li>Hoffmann, K. J. (1836). Doppelte aus dem Klassikern gewählte Beispielsammlung für die Syntax der kleinen und grossen Grammatik von Zumpt: nebst einer Beispielsammlung für die Syntaxis ornata und einem Lesenbuche für Anfänger, Dümmler.</li></ul></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="R">R</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latin_proverbs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: R">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><i>Rapiamus, amici, occasionem de die.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Opportunity knocks only once.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;400. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B400&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Rem tene verba sequentur.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: Stick to the subject and the words will follow. (Marcus Porcius Cato)</li>
<li>Colish, M. L. (1985). The Stoic Tradition from Antiquity to the Early Middle Ages, E.J. Brill.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Repetita iuvant.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "Repetition is useful", or "Repeating things helps”.</li>
<li>Ghislotti, S. (2008). Repetita iuvant. Mnemotecniche del film narrativo, Sestante.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Repetitio est mater studiorum.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: Repetition is the mother of study.</li>
<li>Stone, J. R. (2005). The Routledge Dictionary of Latin Quotations: The Illiterati's Guide to Latin Maxims, Mottoes, Proverbs and Sayings, Routledge.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Roma die uno non aedificata est</i>
<ul><li>Translation: Rome wasn't built in a day.</li>
<li>Kudla, H. (2001). Lexikon der lateinischen Zitate: 3500 Originale mit Übersetzungen und Belegstellen, Beck.</li></ul></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="S">S</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latin_proverbs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: S">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><i>Salus aegroti suprema lex.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: The well-being of the patient is the most important law.</li>
<li>Source: <cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFGiesen1988">Giesen, Dieter&#32;(1988).&#32;<i>International Medical Malpractice Law: A Comparative Law Study of Civil Liability Arising from Medical Care</i>. BRILL. p.&#160;457. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/3166453229" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 3166453229</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=International+Medical+Malpractice+Law%3A+A+Comparative+Law+Study+of+Civil+Liability+Arising+from+Medical+Care&amp;rft.aulast=Giesen&amp;rft.aufirst=Dieter&amp;rft.au=Giesen%2C+Dieter&amp;rft.date=1988&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B457&amp;rft.pub=BRILL&amp;rft.isbn=3166453229&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Salus populi suprema lex esto.</i>
<ul><li>Let the welfare of the people be the supreme law. (motto of the U.S. state of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Missouri" class="extiw" title="w:Missouri">Missouri</a>).</li>
<li>"Ideally, our rules should be formed in such a fashion that an ordinary helpful kind thoughtful person doesn't really even need to know the rules. You just get to work, do something fun, and nobody hassles you as long as you are being thoughtful and kind."</li>
<li>Jimbo Wales, <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia_talk:Ignore_all_rules/Archive_1#from_User_talk:Jimbo_Wales">User talk statement (7 April 2005)</a></li>
<li>Source: <cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFGiesen1988">Giesen, Dieter&#32;(1988).&#32;<i>International Medical Malpractice Law: A Comparative Law Study of Civil Liability Arising from Medical Care</i>. BRILL. p.&#160;457. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/3166453229" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 3166453229</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=International+Medical+Malpractice+Law%3A+A+Comparative+Law+Study+of+Civil+Liability+Arising+from+Medical+Care&amp;rft.aulast=Giesen&amp;rft.aufirst=Dieter&amp;rft.au=Giesen%2C+Dieter&amp;rft.date=1988&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B457&amp;rft.pub=BRILL&amp;rft.isbn=3166453229&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Sapere aude.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: Dare to be wise. (Horace) (Motto of the University of New Brunswick)</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFZanda2004">Zanda, Rubene&#32;(2004).&#32;<i>Sapere aude!: critical thinking in university studies in Latvia</i>. pp.&#160;135. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9984770648" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 9984770648</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Sapere+aude%21%3A+critical+thinking+in+university+studies+in+Latvia&amp;rft.aulast=Zanda&amp;rft.aufirst=Rubene&amp;rft.au=Zanda%2C+Rubene&amp;rft.date=2004&amp;rft.pages=pp.%26nbsp%3B135&amp;rft.isbn=9984770648&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Sapiens dominabitur astris.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: A wise (man) will rule (or possibly, be ruled by) the stars.</li>
<li>Alt. Translation "A Wise Man Is Limited By The Stars"</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFGlick2005">Glick, Thomas F&#32;(2005).&#32;<i>Medieval Science, Technology, and Medicine: An Encyclopedia</i>. Routledge. p.&#160;62. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415969301" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415969301</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Medieval+Science%2C+Technology%2C+and+Medicine%3A+An+Encyclopedia&amp;rft.aulast=Glick&amp;rft.aufirst=Thomas+F&amp;rft.au=Glick%2C+Thomas+F&amp;rft.date=2005&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B62&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415969301&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Sapiens omnia sua secum portat</i>
<ul><li>Translation: A wise man takes everything he owns with himself. (i.e. in his head, his wealth is his wisdom)</li>
<li>English equivalent: A good mind possess a kingdom.</li>
<li>"Sciences contained in books, (such of them at least as are made up of probable reasonings, without demonstrations), composed as they are of the opinions of many different individuals massed together, are farther removed from truth than the simple inferences which a man of good sense using his natural and unprejudiced judgment draws respecting the matters of his experience."</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9_Descartes" title="René Descartes">René Descartes</a>, <i>Discourse on Method</i>, J. Veitch, trans. (1899), part 2, p. 13.</li></ul></li></ul>
<p><br />
</p>
<ul><li><ul><li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFJ._Henle1980">J. Henle, Robert&#32;(1980).&#32;<i>Latin Grammar</i>. Loyola Press. p.&#160;195. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0829401121" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0829401121</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Latin+Grammar&amp;rft.aulast=J.+Henle&amp;rft.aufirst=Robert&amp;rft.au=J.+Henle%2C+Robert&amp;rft.date=1980&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B195&amp;rft.pub=Loyola+Press&amp;rft.isbn=0829401121&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Sapientia abscondita et thesaurus invisus quae utilitas in utrisque.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: You can't take it with you.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;1013. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B1013&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Sapientia est potentia.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: Wisdom is power.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFGulsun2012">Gulsun, Namik&#32;(2012).&#32;<i>Master of Puppets: Seeds of Fate</i>. AuthorHouse. p.&#160;99. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/1467881694" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 1467881694</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Master+of+Puppets%3A+Seeds+of+Fate&amp;rft.aulast=Gulsun&amp;rft.aufirst=Namik&amp;rft.au=Gulsun%2C+Namik&amp;rft.date=2012&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B99&amp;rft.pub=AuthorHouse&amp;rft.isbn=1467881694&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Scientia non habet inimicum nisi ignorantem.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: Knowledge has no enemies but the ignorant.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMilton_Martin1980">Milton Martin, Richard&#32;(1980).&#32;<i>Primordiality, Science, and Value</i>. SUNY Press. p.&#160;148. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0873954432" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0873954432</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Primordiality%2C+Science%2C+and+Value&amp;rft.aulast=Milton+Martin&amp;rft.aufirst=Richard&amp;rft.au=Milton+Martin%2C+Richard&amp;rft.date=1980&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B148&amp;rft.pub=SUNY+Press&amp;rft.isbn=0873954432&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Senatores boni viri, senatus autem mala bestia</i>
<ul><li>Translation: Senators are good men, however Senate is a malicious animal</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFSedláček2011">Sedláček, Tomáš&#32;(2011).&#32;<i>Economics of Good and Evil: The Quest for Economic Meaning from Gilgamesh to Wall Street</i>. Oxford University Press. p.&#160;266. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0199767203" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0199767203</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Economics+of+Good+and+Evil%3A+The+Quest+for+Economic+Meaning+from+Gilgamesh+to+Wall+Street&amp;rft.aulast=Sedl%C3%A1%C4%8Dek&amp;rft.aufirst=Tom%C3%A1%C5%A1&amp;rft.au=Sedl%C3%A1%C4%8Dek%2C+Tom%C3%A1%C5%A1&amp;rft.date=2011&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B266&amp;rft.pub=Oxford+University+Press&amp;rft.isbn=0199767203&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Sermo hominum mores et celat et indicat idem.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Men talk only to conceal the mind.</li>
<li>Source: <cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emmanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European Proverbs, Volym 1</i>. Routledge. p.&#160;1088. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+Proverbs%2C+Volym+1&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emmanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emmanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B1088&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Sepem vir calcat ibi plus ubi passio exstat.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Men leap over where the hedge is lower.</li>
<li>Note: Also knows as the Law of least effort.</li>
<li>Meaning: Always do things in a way that requires the absolut least amount of labor.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;1087. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B1087&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Serpens, nisi serpentem comederit, non fit draco.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: A serpent, if it does not devour a serpent, does not become a dragon.</li>
<li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Francis_Bacon" class="extiw" title="w:Francis Bacon">Francis Bacon</a>, <i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=uVRaAAAAMAAJ&amp;dq=francis%20bacon%20essays%201612&amp;pg=PA374#v=snippet&amp;q=serpens%20nifi%20ser%20pentem%20comederit%20non%20fit%20draco&amp;f=false">Essays</a></i> (1612), apparently translating a <a href="/wiki/Greek_proverbs#.CE.9F" title="Greek proverbs">Greek proverb</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-nares_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nares-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michael_Apostolius" class="extiw" title="w:Michael Apostolius">Michael Apostolius</a>, <i>Proverbs</i> (15th century), translates the Greek proverb: <i>Serpens nisi serpentem edat, non fiet draco.</i><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Erasmus" class="mw-redirect" title="Erasmus">Erasmus</a>, <i>Adages</i> (16th century), translates the Greek proverb: <i>Serpens ni edat serpentem, draco non fiet</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Attributed to <a href="/wiki/Pliny_the_Elder" title="Pliny the Elder">Pliny the Elder</a> (<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_History_(Pliny)" class="extiw" title="w:Natural History (Pliny)">Natural History</a></i>, c. 77-79 AD) by Richard Brathwaite,<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> but Robert Nares believes Brathwaite is mistaken.<sup id="cite_ref-nares_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nares-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> A search of the text returns many remarks on dragons and serpents, but nothing like this statement.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Si cazares, no te alabes; si no cazares, no te enfades.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: If fortune favours, beware of being exalted; if fortune thunders, beware of being overwhelmed.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;1001. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B1001&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Si fueris Romae, Romano vivito more, si fueris alibi, vivito sicut ibi.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: If you are in Rome, live in the Roman way, if you are somewhere else, live like there. (attributed to <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ambrose" class="extiw" title="w:Ambrose">Ambrose of Milan</a>)</li>
<li>English equivalent: When in Rome, do as the Romans.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emmanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European Proverbs, Volym 1</i>. Routledge. p.&#160;673. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+Proverbs%2C+Volym+1&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emmanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emmanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B673&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Si hîc esses, seires qua me vellicent.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: No one knows where the shoe pinches, but he who wears it.</li>
<li>Meaning: "Nobody can fully understand another person's hardship or suffering."</li>
<li>Source for meaning of English equivalent: <cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMartin_H._Manser2007">Martin H. Manser&#32;(2007).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=fgaUQc8NbTYC">The Facts on File Dictionary of Proverbs</a></i>. <li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMawr1885">Mawr, E.B.&#32;(1885).&#32;<i>Analogous Proverbs in Ten Languages</i>. p.&#160;4.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Analogous+Proverbs+in+Ten+Languages&amp;rft.aulast=Mawr&amp;rft.aufirst=E.B.&amp;rft.au=Mawr%2C+E.B.&amp;rft.date=1885&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B4&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>

<ul><li>Translation: "Greatness from Small Beginnings."</li>

<ul><li><i>Similia similibus.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Like will to like.</li>
<li>"Every man loves well what is <i>like</i> to himself."</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book"><i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=fXrlvr_kPXwC&amp;pg=PA216">Folk-Etymology</a></i>. <li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMawr1885">Mawr, E.B.&#32;(1885).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://editura.mttlc.ro/carti/mawr-analogous-proverbs.pdf">Analogous Proverbs in Ten Languages</a></i>. p.&#160;51.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Analogous+Proverbs+in+Ten+Languages&amp;rft.aulast=Mawr&amp;rft.aufirst=E.B.&amp;rft.au=Mawr%2C+E.B.&amp;rft.date=1885&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B51&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Feditura.mttlc.ro%2Fcarti%2Fmawr-analogous-proverbs.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Si vis pacem, para bellum.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "If you want peace, prepare for war."</li>
<li>Paraphrase of <i>Igitur qui desiderat pacem, praeparet bellum</i> (<a href="/wiki/Vegetius" class="mw-redirect" title="Vegetius">Vegetius</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/De_Re_Militari" class="extiw" title="w:De Re Militari"><i>Epitoma rei militaris</i></a>)</li>
<li>Origin of the name <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/parabellum" class="extiw" title="w:parabellum">parabellum</a></i> for some ammunition and firearms, e.g. <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luger" class="extiw" title="w:Luger">Luger</a> parabellum</li>
