<ul><li><i>Si vis pacem, para iustitiam.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "If you want peace, prepare justice."</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFKeogh2008">Keogh, Dermot&#32;(2008).&#32;<i>Gerald Goldberg: A Tribute</i>. Mercier Press Ltd. p.&#160;169. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/1856355810" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 1856355810</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Gerald+Goldberg%3A+A+Tribute&amp;rft.aulast=Keogh&amp;rft.aufirst=Dermot&amp;rft.au=Keogh%2C+Dermot&amp;rft.date=2008&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B169&amp;rft.pub=Mercier+Press+Ltd&amp;rft.isbn=1856355810&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Silent enim leges inter arma</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "Laws are silent in times of war"</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFCryer2010">Cryer, Friman&#32;(2010).&#32;<i>An Introduction to International Criminal Law and Procedure</i>. Cambridge University Press. p.&#160;270. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0521135818" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0521135818</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=An+Introduction+to+International+Criminal+Law+and+Procedure&amp;rft.aulast=Cryer&amp;rft.aufirst=Friman&amp;rft.au=Cryer%2C+Friman&amp;rft.date=2010&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B270&amp;rft.pub=Cambridge+University+Press&amp;rft.isbn=0521135818&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Simia est simia, etiasmi purpura vestiatur.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: "A golden bit does not make the horse any better."</li>
<li>Meaning: An ugly thing will remain ugly even if its appeareance is taken care of.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1998">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1998).&#32;<i>Concise Dictionary of European Proverbs</i>&#32;(Abbreviated ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;52. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415160502" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415160502</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Concise+Dictionary+of+European+Proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1998&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B52&amp;rft.edition=Abbreviated&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415160502&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>Some remedies are worse than the disease.
<ul><li>Note: Specified as a Roman proverb in the source.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStone2006">Stone&#32;(2006).&#32;<i>Routledge Dictionary of World Proverbs</i>. Taylor \&amp; Francis. p.&#160;357.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Routledge+Dictionary+of+World+Proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Stone&amp;rft.au=Stone&amp;rft.date=2006&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B357&amp;rft.pub=Taylor+%5C%26+Francis&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Stultorum est se alienis immiscere negotiis.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Give neither salt nor counsel till you are asked for it.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMawr1885">Mawr, E.B.&#32;(1885).&#32;<i>Analogous Proverbs in Ten Languages</i>. p.&#160;60.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Analogous+Proverbs+in+Ten+Languages&amp;rft.aulast=Mawr&amp;rft.aufirst=E.B.&amp;rft.au=Mawr%2C+E.B.&amp;rft.date=1885&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B60&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Sua cuique sponsa, mihi mea; suum cuique pulchrum.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Every man thinks his own geese swans.</li>
<li>"This proverb imitates that an inbred <i>Philauty</i> runs through the whole Race of Flefh and Blood. It <i>blinds</i> the Underftanding, <i>perverts</i> the Judgment and <i>depraves</i> the Reafon of the Diftinguishers of Truth and Falfity."</li>
<li><i>Divers Proverbs</i>, Nathan Bailey, 1721 <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://web.archive.org/web/20081123025121/http://www.fromoldbooks.org/proverbs/pages/pp20-21/">[4]</a></li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMawr1885">Mawr, E.B.&#32;(1885).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://editura.mttlc.ro/carti/mawr-analogous-proverbs.pdf">Analogous Proverbs in Ten Languages</a></i>. p.&#160;42.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Analogous+Proverbs+in+Ten+Languages&amp;rft.aulast=Mawr&amp;rft.aufirst=E.B.&amp;rft.au=Mawr%2C+E.B.&amp;rft.date=1885&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B42&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Feditura.mttlc.ro%2Fcarti%2Fmawr-analogous-proverbs.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Summum ius summa inuria.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "More law, less justice." (<a href="/wiki/Cicero" title="Cicero">Cicero</a>, <i>De officiis</i> I, 10, 33)</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFWhittaker2000">Whittaker, Simon&#32;(2000).&#32;<i>Good Faith in European Contract Law</i>. Cambridge University Press. p.&#160;65. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0521771900" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0521771900</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Good+Faith+in+European+Contract+Law&amp;rft.aulast=Whittaker&amp;rft.aufirst=Simon&amp;rft.au=Whittaker%2C+Simon&amp;rft.date=2000&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B65&amp;rft.pub=Cambridge+University+Press&amp;rft.isbn=0521771900&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Sunt facta verbis difficiliora</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "Works are harder than words."</li>
<li>English equivalent: "Easier said than done."</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFShackleton-Bailey2004">Shackleton-Bailey, D. R.&#32;(2004).&#32;<i>Cicero: Epistulae Ad Quintum Fratrem Et M. Brutum</i>. Cambridge University Press. p.&#160;49. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0521607000" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0521607000</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Cicero%3A+Epistulae+Ad+Quintum+Fratrem+Et+M.+Brutum&amp;rft.aulast=Shackleton-Bailey&amp;rft.aufirst=D.+R.&amp;rft.au=Shackleton-Bailey%2C+D.+R.&amp;rft.date=2004&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B49&amp;rft.pub=Cambridge+University+Press&amp;rft.isbn=0521607000&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Sunt pueri pueri pueri puerilia tractant</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "Boys are boys and boys will act like boys."</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStone2005">Stone, Jon R.&#32;(2005).&#32;<i>The Routledge Dictionary of Latin Quotations: The Illiterati's Guide to Latin Maxims, Mottoes, Proverbs and Sayings Latin for the Illiterati Series</i>. Routledge. p.&#160;115. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415969085" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415969085</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Routledge+Dictionary+of+Latin+Quotations%3A+The+Illiterati%27s+Guide+to+Latin+Maxims%2C+Mottoes%2C+Proverbs+and+Sayings+Latin+for+the+Illiterati+Series&amp;rft.aulast=Stone&amp;rft.aufirst=Jon+R.&amp;rft.au=Stone%2C+Jon+R.&amp;rft.date=2005&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B115&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415969085&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li>
<li>English equivalent: Boys will be boys.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Sutor, ne ultra crepidam!</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "Cobbler, no further than the sandal!" I.e. don't offer your opinion on things that are outside your competence. It is said that the Greek painter <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apelles" class="extiw" title="w:Apelles">Apelles</a> once asked the advice of a cobbler on how to render the sandals of a soldier he was painting. When the cobbler started offering advice on other parts of the painting, Apelles rebuked him with this phrase (but in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greek_language" class="extiw" title="w:Greek language">Greek</a>).</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book"><i>Sutor ne ultra crepidam, oder ein jeder bleib bey seinem Handwerck: In einem mit Nachsetzung seines Handwerks allzu weit über die Schnur hauenden Schmidt, zu einem Faßnacht-Hainzl vorgestellt in Seminario Cler. Saec. In Com. Vir. Zu Ingolstadt</i>. 1740.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Sutor+ne+ultra+crepidam%2C+oder+ein+jeder+bleib+bey+seinem+Handwerck%3A+In+einem+mit+Nachsetzung+seines+Handwerks+allzu+weit+%C3%BCber+die+Schnur+hauenden+Schmidt%2C+zu+einem+Fa%C3%9Fnacht-Hainzl+vorgestellt+in+Seminario+Cler.+Saec.+In+Com.+Vir.+Zu+Ingolstadt&amp;rft.date=1740&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Suum cuique Pulchrum.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: To each its own is beautiful.</li>
<li>English equivalent: The bird loves her own nest.</li>
<li><i>Divers Proverbs</i>, Nathan Bailey, 1721 <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://web.archive.org/web/20081123025121/http://www.fromoldbooks.org/proverbs/pages/pp20-21/">[5]</a></li></ul></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="T">T</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latin_proverbs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: T">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><i>Tarde venientibus ossa.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "For those who come late, only the bones."</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European Proverbs, Volym 1</i>. Routledge. p.&#160;625. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+Proverbs%2C+Volym+1&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B625&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Tempora aptari decet.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: Times should be adapted to.</li>
<li>English equivalent: Take things as you find them.</li>
<li>"We should not plan and then try to make circumstances fit those plans. Instead we should make plans fit the circumstances."</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/George_S._Patton" title="George S. Patton">George S. Patton</a>, <i>War as I Knew It</i> (1947)</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;865. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B865&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Tempori parce!</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "Save time!"</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFGottlob_Zumpt1836">Gottlob Zumpt, Karl&#32;(1836).&#32;<i>A grammar of the Latin language</i>&#32;(4 ed.). B. Fellowes. p.&#160;275.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=A+grammar+of+the+Latin+language&amp;rft.aulast=Gottlob+Zumpt&amp;rft.aufirst=Karl&amp;rft.au=Gottlob+Zumpt%2C+Karl&amp;rft.date=1836&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B275&amp;rft.edition=4&amp;rft.pub=B.+Fellowes&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Tempus fugit.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "Time flees." (i.e., "time flies"). Originally as <i>Sed fugit interea, fugit irreparabile tempus</i> - translation: "Meanwhile the irreplaceable time flees" (<a href="/wiki/Virgil" title="Virgil">Virgil</a>)</li>
<li>English equivalent: Time and tide waits for none.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFAlmond2002">Almond, Frank&#32;(2002).&#32;<i>Tempus Fugit</i>. C&amp;M Online Media. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0917990501" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0917990501</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Tempus+Fugit&amp;rft.aulast=Almond&amp;rft.aufirst=Frank&amp;rft.au=Almond%2C+Frank&amp;rft.date=2002&amp;rft.pub=C%26M+Online+Media&amp;rft.isbn=0917990501&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Tempus fugit, aeternitas manet.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "Time flees, eternity dwells."</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European Proverbs, Volume 1</i>&#32;(illustrerad ed.). p.&#160;625. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+Proverbs%2C+Volume+1&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B625&amp;rft.edition=illustrerad&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Tempus fugit, amor manet.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "Time flees, love stays"</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREF(Edith)_Nesbit2010">(Edith) Nesbit, E&#32;(2010).&#32;<i>Man and Maid</i>. Echo Library. p.&#160;10. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/1406895598" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 1406895598</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Man+and+Maid&amp;rft.aulast=%28Edith%29+Nesbit&amp;rft.aufirst=E&amp;rft.au=%28Edith%29+Nesbit%2C+E&amp;rft.date=2010&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B10&amp;rft.pub=Echo+Library&amp;rft.isbn=1406895598&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Timendi causa est nescire.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "The cause of fear is ignorance." (<a href="/wiki/Seneca" class="mw-disambig" title="Seneca">Seneca</a>)</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFR._Stone2005">R. Stone, Jon&#32;(2005).&#32;<i>The Routledge Dictionary of Latin Quotations: The Illiterati's Guide to Latin Maxims, Mottoes, Proverbs and Sayings</i>&#32;(illustrerad ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;118. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415969093" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415969093</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Routledge+Dictionary+of+Latin+Quotations%3A+The+Illiterati%27s+Guide+to+Latin+Maxims%2C+Mottoes%2C+Proverbs+and+Sayings&amp;rft.aulast=R.+Stone&amp;rft.aufirst=Jon&amp;rft.au=R.+Stone%2C+Jon&amp;rft.date=2005&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B118&amp;rft.edition=illustrerad&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415969093&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Tres faciunt collegium.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "Three makes a company."</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFBerger1953">Berger, Adolf&#32;(1953).&#32;<i>Encyclopedic Dictionary of Roman Law, Volym 43 Transactions of the American Philosophical Society</i>. American Philosophical Society. p.&#160;742. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0871694328" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0871694328</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Encyclopedic+Dictionary+of+Roman+Law%2C+Volym+43+Transactions+of+the+American+Philosophical+Society&amp;rft.aulast=Berger&amp;rft.aufirst=Adolf&amp;rft.au=Berger%2C+Adolf&amp;rft.date=1953&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B742&amp;rft.pub=American+Philosophical+Society&amp;rft.isbn=0871694328&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Tolle, lege; Tolle, lege!</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "Take up and read; take up and read!" (<a href="/w/index.php?title=Augustinus&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Augustinus (page does not exist)">Augustinus</a>)</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFJ._Teske2011">J. Teske, Roland&#32;(2011).&#32;<i>Tolle Lege: Essays on Augustine and on Medieval Philosophy in Honor of Roland J. Teske, Sj Utgåva 73 av Marquette Studies in Philosophy</i>. Marquette University Press. pp.&#160;364. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0874628075" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0874628075</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Tolle+Lege%3A+Essays+on+Augustine+and+on+Medieval+Philosophy+in+Honor+of+Roland+J.+Teske%2C+Sj+Utg%C3%A5va+73+av+Marquette+Studies+in+Philosophy&amp;rft.aulast=J.+Teske&amp;rft.aufirst=Roland&amp;rft.au=J.+Teske%2C+Roland&amp;rft.date=2011&amp;rft.pages=pp.%26nbsp%3B364&amp;rft.pub=Marquette+University+Press&amp;rft.isbn=0874628075&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Tunc tua res agitur, paries cum proximus ardet.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "It also concerns you when the nearest wall is burning."</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFR._Stone2005">R. Stone, Jon&#32;(2005).&#32;<i>The Routledge Dictionary of Latin Quotations: The Illiterati's Guide to Latin Maxims, Mottoes, Proverbs and Sayings</i>&#32;(illustrerad ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;119. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415969093" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415969093</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Routledge+Dictionary+of+Latin+Quotations%3A+The+Illiterati%27s+Guide+to+Latin+Maxims%2C+Mottoes%2C+Proverbs+and+Sayings&amp;rft.aulast=R.+Stone&amp;rft.aufirst=Jon&amp;rft.au=R.+Stone%2C+Jon&amp;rft.date=2005&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B119&amp;rft.edition=illustrerad&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415969093&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="U">U</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latin_proverbs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: U">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li>Ut salutas (saltus), ita salutaberis oder Malo arboris nodo malus clavus and cuneus infigendus est.
<ul><li>English equivalent: What goes around comes around.</li>
<li>Meaning: Good acts quite often reward themselves. Conversely, bad acts quite often punish themselves.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFLautenbach2002">Lautenbach, Ernst&#32;(2002).&#32;<i>Latein-Deutsch: Zitaten-Lexikon: Quellennachweise</i>. LIT Verlag Münster. p.&#160;646. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/3825856526" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 3825856526</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Latein-Deutsch%3A+Zitaten-Lexikon%3A+Quellennachweise&amp;rft.aulast=Lautenbach&amp;rft.aufirst=Ernst&amp;rft.au=Lautenbach%2C+Ernst&amp;rft.date=2002&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B646&amp;rft.pub=LIT+Verlag+M%C3%BCnster&amp;rft.isbn=3825856526&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Ubi bene, ibi patria</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "Where one feels good, there is one's country."</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFAdeleye1999">Adeleye, Gabriel&#32;(1999).&#32;<i>World Dictionary of Foreign Expressions: A Resource for Readers and Writers</i>. Bolchazy-Carducci Publishers. p.&#160;389. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0865164231" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0865164231</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=World+Dictionary+of+Foreign+Expressions%3A+A+Resource+for+Readers+and+Writers&amp;rft.aulast=Adeleye&amp;rft.aufirst=Gabriel&amp;rft.au=Adeleye%2C+Gabriel&amp;rft.date=1999&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B389&amp;rft.pub=Bolchazy-Carducci+Publishers&amp;rft.isbn=0865164231&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Ubi concordia, ibi victoria.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "Where there is harmony, there is victory."</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFWebb2006">Webb, Amy&#32;(2006).&#32;<i>The Devil's Duty</i>. Lulu.com. pp.&#160;212. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/1411649842" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 1411649842</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Devil%27s+Duty&amp;rft.aulast=Webb&amp;rft.aufirst=Amy&amp;rft.au=Webb%2C+Amy&amp;rft.date=2006&amp;rft.pages=pp.%26nbsp%3B212&amp;rft.pub=Lulu.com&amp;rft.isbn=1411649842&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Ubi dubium, ibi libertas.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "Where there is doubt, there is freedom." legal, meaning when in doubt the prisoner has to be freed.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFGreener2006">Greener, Richard&#32;(2006).&#32;<i>The Lacey Confession</i>. Llewellyn Worldwide. p.&#160;420. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0738708704" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0738708704</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Lacey+Confession&amp;rft.aulast=Greener&amp;rft.aufirst=Richard&amp;rft.au=Greener%2C+Richard&amp;rft.date=2006&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B420&amp;rft.pub=Llewellyn+Worldwide&amp;rft.isbn=0738708704&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Ubi fumus, ibi ignis.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "Where there's smoke, there's fire."</li>
<li>Meaning: Where there are the signs of something, something is there.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFThomasius1715">Thomasius, Christian&#32;(1715).&#32;<i>Cautelae circa doctrinam de praesumptione allodialitatis</i>. p.&#160;29.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Cautelae+circa+doctrinam+de+praesumptione+allodialitatis&amp;rft.aulast=Thomasius&amp;rft.aufirst=Christian&amp;rft.au=Thomasius%2C+Christian&amp;rft.date=1715&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B29&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Ulula cum lupis, cum quibus esse cupis.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "Who keeps company with wolves, will learn to howl."</li>
<li>Meaning: You will become like the people you surround yourself with.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFTournoy1993">Tournoy, Gilbert&#32;(1993).&#32;<i>Humanistica Lovaniensia</i>. Leuven University Press. p.&#160;32. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9061865719" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 9061865719</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Humanistica+Lovaniensia&amp;rft.aulast=Tournoy&amp;rft.aufirst=Gilbert&amp;rft.au=Tournoy%2C+Gilbert&amp;rft.date=1993&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B32&amp;rft.pub=Leuven+University+Press&amp;rft.isbn=9061865719&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Uni navi ne committas omnia.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: Do not commit all to one boat.</li>
<li>English equivalent: Don't put all your eggs in the same basket.</li>
<li>Meaning: "Spread your risks or investments so that if one enterprise fails you will not lose everything."</li>
<li>Source for meaning of English equivalent: <cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMartin_H._Manser2007">Martin H. Manser&#32;(2007).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=fgaUQc8NbTYC&amp;pg=PA63">The Facts on File Dictionary of Proverbs</a></i>. Infobase Publishing. p.&#160;63. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780816066735" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 978-0-8160-6673-5</a><span class="reference-accessdate">.&#32;Retrieved on 18 August 2013</span>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Facts+on+File+Dictionary+of+Proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Martin+H.+Manser&amp;rft.au=Martin+H.+Manser&amp;rft.date=2007&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B63&amp;rft.pub=Infobase+Publishing&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-8160-6673-5&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DfgaUQc8NbTYC%26pg%3DPA63&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;715. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B715&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Una hirundo non facit ver</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "One swallow doesn't make spring"</li>
<li>Meaning: A solitary event is no indication that a major change is taking place.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFVergil1663">Vergil, Polydore&#32;(1663).&#32;<i>Polydori Virgilii De Rerum Inventoribus</i>&#32;(nytryck ed.). Ayer Publishing. p.&#160;xii. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0833715631" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0833715631</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Polydori+Virgilii+De+Rerum+Inventoribus&amp;rft.aulast=Vergil&amp;rft.aufirst=Polydore&amp;rft.au=Vergil%2C+Polydore&amp;rft.date=1663&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3Bxii&amp;rft.edition=nytryck&amp;rft.pub=Ayer+Publishing&amp;rft.isbn=0833715631&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Unum castigabis, centum emendabis.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: For one reprimand, a hundred corrections."</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFLautenbach2002">Lautenbach, Ernst&#32;(2002).&#32;<i>Latein-Deutsch: Zitaten-Lexikon: Quellennachweise</i>. LIT Verlag Münster. p.&#160;129. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/3825856526" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 3825856526</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Latein-Deutsch%3A+Zitaten-Lexikon%3A+Quellennachweise&amp;rft.aulast=Lautenbach&amp;rft.aufirst=Ernst&amp;rft.au=Lautenbach%2C+Ernst&amp;rft.date=2002&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B129&amp;rft.pub=LIT+Verlag+M%C3%BCnster&amp;rft.isbn=3825856526&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Usus magister est optimus.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "Experience is the best teacher."  (i.e., "Practice makes perfect.")</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emmanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European Proverbs, Volym 1</i>. Routledge. p.&#160;698. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+Proverbs%2C+Volym+1&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emmanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emmanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B698&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Ut ameris, amabilis esto.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "Be amiable, then you'll be loved."</li>
<li>Stone, J. R. (2005). The Routledge Dictionary of Latin Quotations: The Illiterati's Guide to Latin Maxims, Mottoes, Proverbs and Sayings, Routledge.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Ut desint vires, tamen est laudanda voluntas</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "Even if the powers are missing, the will deserves praise" (<a href="/wiki/Ovid" title="Ovid">Ovid</a>)</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFKirk_Rappaport2005">Kirk Rappaport, Pamela&#32;(2005).&#32;<i>Sor Juana Inés de la Cruz: Selected Writings</i>. Paulist Press. p.&#160;290. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0809105306" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0809105306</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Sor+Juana+In%C3%A9s+de+la+Cruz%3A+Selected+Writings&amp;rft.aulast=Kirk+Rappaport&amp;rft.aufirst=Pamela&amp;rft.au=Kirk+Rappaport%2C+Pamela&amp;rft.date=2005&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B290&amp;rft.pub=Paulist+Press&amp;rft.isbn=0809105306&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Ut sementem feceris, ita metes.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "You'll reap what you sow." (<a href="/wiki/Cicero" title="Cicero">Cicero</a>, "De oratore"); <a href="/wiki/The_Bible" title="The Bible">The Bible</a> Job 4:8; Galatians 6:7.</li>
<li>English equivalent: What you reap is what you sow.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFSloman1928">Sloman, Arthur&#32;(1928).&#32;<i>a grammar of classical latin</i>. CUP Archive. p.&#160;343.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=a+grammar+of+classical+latin&amp;rft.aulast=Sloman&amp;rft.aufirst=Arthur&amp;rft.au=Sloman%2C+Arthur&amp;rft.date=1928&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B343&amp;rft.pub=CUP+Archive&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Ut sis nocte levis, sit cena brevis!</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "That your sleeping hour be peaceful, let your dining hour be brief!" (<i>Sis</i> is one hour before sunset.) (modern: Sleep hard, Sleep fast, Sleep well)</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emmanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European Proverbs, Volym 1</i>. Routledge. p.&#160;818. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+Proverbs%2C+Volym+1&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emmanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emmanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B818&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Uxor formosa et vinum sunt dulcia venena.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: "Beautiful women and wine are sweet venom."</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFBeudel1911">Beudel, Paul&#32;(1911).&#32;<i>Qua ratione Graeci liberos docuerint, papyris, ostracis, tabulis in Aegypto inventis illustratur: commentationem philologicam</i>. E Typographia Aschendorffiana. p.&#160;32.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Qua+ratione+Graeci+liberos+docuerint%2C+papyris%2C+ostracis%2C+tabulis+in+Aegypto+inventis+illustratur%3A+commentationem+philologicam&amp;rft.aulast=Beudel&amp;rft.aufirst=Paul&amp;rft.au=Beudel%2C+Paul&amp;rft.date=1911&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B32&amp;rft.pub=E+Typographia+Aschendorffiana&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="V">V</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latin_proverbs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: V">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><i>Varitatio delectat</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Variety is the spice of life.</li>
<li>Source: <cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1998">Strauss, Emmanuel&#32;(1998).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European Proverbs</i>. Routledge. p.&#160;89. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415160502" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415160502</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+Proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emmanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emmanuel&amp;rft.date=1998&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B89&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415160502&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Vasa vana plurimum sonant</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: It is not the hen that cackles the most that lay the most eggs.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMacdonnel1869">Macdonnel, David Evans&#32;(1869).&#32;<i>A dictionary of select and popular quotations, which are in daily use: taken from the Latin, French, Greek, Spanish and Italian languages&#160;: together with a copious collection of law-maxims and law-terms translated into English, with illustrations historical and idiomatic</i>&#32;(6 ed.). Claxton, Remsen &amp; Haffelfinger. p.&#160;296.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=A+dictionary+of+select+and+popular+quotations%2C+which+are+in+daily+use%3A+taken+from+the+Latin%2C+French%2C+Greek%2C+Spanish+and+Italian+languages+%3A+together+with+a+copious+collection+of+law-maxims+and+law-terms+translated+into+English%2C+with+illustrations+historical+and+idiomatic&amp;rft.aulast=Macdonnel&amp;rft.aufirst=David+Evans&amp;rft.au=Macdonnel%2C+David+Evans&amp;rft.date=1869&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B296&amp;rft.edition=6&amp;rft.pub=Claxton%2C+Remsen+%26+Haffelfinger&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Ventis secundis, tene cursum.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Go with the flow.</li>
<li>"Water shapes its course according to the nature of the ground over which it flows. Let your methods be regulated by the infinite variety of circumstances."</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFTzũ¨_400_B.C">Tzu, Sun&#32;(̃¨ 400 B.C).&#32;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://classics.mit.edu/Tzu/artwar.html">"VI. Weak Points and Strong"</a>.&#32;<i>The Art of War</i>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.btitle=VI.+Weak+Points+and+Strong&amp;rft.atitle=The+Art+of+War&amp;rft.aulast=Tzu&amp;rft.aufirst=Sun&amp;rft.au=Tzu%2C+Sun&amp;rft.date=%CC%83%C2%A8+400+B.C&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fclassics.mit.edu%2FTzu%2Fartwar.html&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMesiah2007">Mesiah, Leza M.&#32;(2007).&#32;<i>Recipes for Recovery: How to Heal Loss and a Broken Heart</i>. AuthorHouse. p.&#160;138. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/1425965954" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 1425965954</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Recipes+for+Recovery%3A+How+to+Heal+Loss+and+a+Broken+Heart&amp;rft.aulast=Mesiah&amp;rft.aufirst=Leza+M.&amp;rft.au=Mesiah%2C+Leza+M.&amp;rft.date=2007&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B138&amp;rft.pub=AuthorHouse&amp;rft.isbn=1425965954&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Verba docent, exempla trahunt.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: Words instruct, illustrations lead.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFRautenberg2009">Rautenberg, Wolfgang&#32;(2009).&#32;<i>A Concise Introduction to Mathematical Logi</i>&#32;(3, illustrerad ed.). Springer. p.&#160;58. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/1441912207" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 1441912207</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=A+Concise+Introduction+to+Mathematical+Logi&amp;rft.aulast=Rautenberg&amp;rft.aufirst=Wolfgang&amp;rft.au=Rautenberg%2C+Wolfgang&amp;rft.date=2009&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B58&amp;rft.edition=3%2C+illustrerad&amp;rft.pub=Springer&amp;rft.isbn=1441912207&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Verba volant, scripta manent.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: Paper is forbearing.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFC._Gerhart1998">C. Gerhart, Eugene&#32;(1998).&#32;<i>Quote It Completely!: World Reference Guide to More Than 5,500 Memorable Quotations from Law and Literature Quote it Completely!: World Reference Guide to More Than 5,500 Memorable Quotations from Law and Literature, Eugene C. Gerhart,</i>. Wm. S. Hein Publishing. p.&#160;1171. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/1575884003" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 1575884003</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Quote+It+Completely%21%3A+World+Reference+Guide+to+More+Than+5%2C500+Memorable+Quotations+from+Law+and+Literature+Quote+it+Completely%21%3A+World+Reference+Guide+to+More+Than+5%2C500+Memorable+Quotations+from+Law+and+Literature%2C+Eugene+C.+Gerhart%2C&amp;rft.aulast=C.+Gerhart&amp;rft.aufirst=Eugene&amp;rft.au=C.+Gerhart%2C+Eugene&amp;rft.date=1998&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B1171&amp;rft.pub=Wm.+S.+Hein+Publishing&amp;rft.isbn=1575884003&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Verit eo caudam, qua decidit arbore, malum.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: The apple does not fall far from the tree.</li>
<li>"Children observe daily and — in their behaviour — often follow the example of their parents."</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFPaczolay1997">Paczolay, Gyula&#32;(1997).&#32;<i>European Proverbs in 55 languages</i>. DeProverbio.com. p.&#160;259. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/1875943447" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 1-875943-44-7</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=European+Proverbs+in+55+languages&amp;rft.aulast=Paczolay&amp;rft.aufirst=Gyula&amp;rft.au=Paczolay%2C+Gyula&amp;rft.date=1997&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B259&amp;rft.pub=DeProverbio.com&amp;rft.isbn=1-875943-44-7&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Veritas odium paret</i>
<ul><li>Translation: Truth creates hatred. (<a href="/wiki/Terence" title="Terence">Terence</a>, Andria 68)</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFSacul2011">Sacul, Snofla&#32;(2011).&#32;<i>If Only God Used His Brain: Ahead of Time</i>. Xlibris Corporation. p.&#160;149. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/146533565X" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 146533565X</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=If+Only+God+Used+His+Brain%3A+Ahead+of+Time&amp;rft.aulast=Sacul&amp;rft.aufirst=Snofla&amp;rft.au=Sacul%2C+Snofla&amp;rft.date=2011&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B149&amp;rft.pub=Xlibris+Corporation&amp;rft.isbn=146533565X&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Veritas vos liberabit</i>
<ul><li>Translation: The truth will set you free.</li>
<li>From the <i>Gospel of John</i>, 8:32</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFR._Stone2013">R. Stone, Jon&#32;(2013).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=EZJoSq45EPQC&amp;pg=PA217">The Routledge Dictionary of Latin Quotations: The Illiterati's Guide to Latin Maxims, Mottoes, Proverbs, and Sayings</a></i>. p.&#160;217. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9781135881108" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 978-1-135-88110-8</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Routledge+Dictionary+of+Latin+Quotations%3A+The+Illiterati%27s+Guide+to+Latin+Maxims%2C+Mottoes%2C+Proverbs%2C+and+Sayings&amp;rft.aulast=R.+Stone&amp;rft.aufirst=Jon&amp;rft.au=R.+Stone%2C+Jon&amp;rft.date=2013&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B217&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-135-88110-8&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DEZJoSq45EPQC%26pg%3DPA217&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Veritatem dies aperit.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: Time discloses the truth.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emmanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European Proverbs, Volym 1</i>. Routledge. p.&#160;1206. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+Proverbs%2C+Volym+1&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emmanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emmanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B1206&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Vincit omnia veritas.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: Truth conquers all.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStone1996">Stone, Jon R.&#32;(1996).&#32;<i>Latin for the Illiterati: Exorcizing the Ghosts of a Dead Language Classics, Language, Reference</i>. Routledge. p.&#160;150. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415917751" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415917751</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Latin+for+the+Illiterati%3A+Exorcizing+the+Ghosts+of+a+Dead+Language+Classics%2C+Language%2C+Reference&amp;rft.aulast=Stone&amp;rft.aufirst=Jon+R.&amp;rft.au=Stone%2C+Jon+R.&amp;rft.date=1996&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B150&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415917751&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Vincit qui patitur.</i> - motto Berea College, Berea, KY
<ul><li>English equivalent: Persevere and never fear.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFOlive_Emmons2009">Olive Emmons, Mary&#32;(2009).&#32;<i>Moods and Whims</i>. READ BOOKS. p.&#160;53. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/1444678787" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 1444678787</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Moods+and+Whims&amp;rft.aulast=Olive+Emmons&amp;rft.aufirst=Mary&amp;rft.au=Olive+Emmons%2C+Mary&amp;rft.date=2009&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B53&amp;rft.pub=READ+BOOKS&amp;rft.isbn=1444678787&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Vipera in veprecula est.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent:  Look before you leap, for snakes among sweet flowers do creep.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFStrauss1994">Strauss, Emanuel&#32;(1994).&#32;<i>Dictionary of European proverbs</i>&#32;(Volume 2 ed.). Routledge. p.&#160;1070. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B1070&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Vir fugiens et denuo pugnabit.</i>
<ul><li>English equivalent: He who fights and runs away may live to fight another day.</li>
<li>"It is wiser to withdraw from a situation that you cannot win than to go on fighting and lose – by a strategic retreat you can return to the battle or argument with renewed energy at a later date."</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFMartin_H._Manser2007">Martin H. Manser&#32;(2007).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=fgaUQc8NbTYC&amp;pg=PA123">The Facts on File Dictionary of Proverbs</a></i>. Routledge. p.&#160;702. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0415096243" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0415096243</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+European+proverbs&amp;rft.aulast=Strauss&amp;rft.aufirst=Emanuel&amp;rft.au=Strauss%2C+Emanuel&amp;rft.date=1994&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B702&amp;rft.edition=Volume+2&amp;rft.pub=Routledge&amp;rft.isbn=0415096243&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Viveri bis, vitâ posse priori frui.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: It is to live twice to be able to enjoy the retrospect of your past life.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFHugh_Moore1831">Hugh Moore&#32;(1831).&#32;<i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=2wb-dMzaXw8C&amp;pg=PA61">A dictionary of quotations from various authors in ancient and modern languages</a></i>. p.&#160;137<span class="reference-accessdate">.&#32;Retrieved on 14 August 2013</span>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=A+dictionary+of+quotations+from+various+authors+in+ancient+and+modern+languages&amp;rft.aulast=Hugh+Moore&amp;rft.au=Hugh+Moore&amp;rft.date=1831&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B137&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3D2wb-dMzaXw8C%26pg%3DPA61&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><i>Vivit post funera virtus.</i>
<ul><li>Translation: Virtue survives the grave.</li>
<li><cite style="font-style:normal" class="book" id="CITEREFHenry_Thomas_Riley1856">Henry Thomas Riley&#32;(1856).&#32;<i>Dictionary of Latin Quotations, Proverbs, Maxims, and Mottos, Classical and Mediaeval</i>. p.&#160;503.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Dictionary+of+Latin+Quotations%2C+Proverbs%2C+Maxims%2C+and+Mottos%2C+Classical+and+Mediaeval&amp;rft.aulast=Henry+Thomas+Riley&amp;rft.au=Henry+Thomas+Riley&amp;rft.date=1856&amp;rft.pages=p.%26nbsp%3B503&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Latin_proverbs"><span style="display: none;">&#160;</span></span></li></ul></li></ul>

<ul><li>English equivalent A leopard won't change its spots.</li>

<li id="cite_note-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-5">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text">Erasmus III iii 61, translated in William Watson Barker, ed. <i>The Adages of Erasmus</i>, p. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=VmJn6IFMyicC&amp;lpg=PA272&amp;dq=Apostolius%20drakon&amp;pg=PA272#v=onepage&amp;q=Serpens%20ni%20edat%20serpentem,%20draco%20non%20fiet&amp;f=false">272</a></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-6"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-6">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text">Richard Brathwaite, <i>The English Gentleman</i> 1630, p. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://gateway.proquest.com/openurl?ctx_ver=Z39.88-2003&amp;res_id=xri:eebo&amp;rft_id=xri:eebo:image:4869:129">237</a>.</span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
